Tiger Woods, a 14-time major champion, trails fellow American JB Holmes by nine strokes after the first round of a tournament he hosts for his charitable foundation. Woods, aged 40, recorded four birdies in his first eight holes but bogeyed the ninth and 11th, and doubled bogeyed the 16th and 18th for a score of one over par. He expressed satisfaction with his performance, stating he "felt good" and is "looking forward to the next few days." Woods attributed his mistakes to errant drives and difficult chip shots, lamenting the shots he hit into bushes and water. His first double bogey came after a wayward approach shot on the 16th, followed by an over-hit fourth and two putts from the back edge. On the 18th, he drove into a lake and two-putted from 12 feet for another double bogey. Despite these late errors, Woods had briefly tied for the lead at four under after a run of three birdies from the sixth hole. Holmes leads the 18-man field with an impressive eight-under-par 64, which included seven birdies and an eagle. Hideki Matsuyama of Japan is a shot behind Holmes, with Dustin Johnson, the US Open winner, one further back on six under. The Open champion, Henrik Stenson, along with Matt Kuchar, Louis Oosthuizen, and Justin Rose, the Olympic champion, finished the first round tied for fourth on five under. Rose, who has taken a seven-week break, currently lags behind the field at two over par.
The official Oman News Agency announced that three Americans were flown out of Sanaa, the Yemeni capital controlled by the Houthi rebel group, on Wednesday. The U.S. government had requested Oman's assistance in locating them, the agency added. The Omani ministry did not disclose the Americans' identities, but a Yemeni security official informed Reuters that they had been held by the rebels. According to the official, who spoke by phone from Sanaa, the three Americans were detained by the Houthi security forces on suspicion of spying. Earlier this month, the U.S. State Department reported that an American contractor for the United Nations who was detained at Sanaa airport last month had passed away. John Hamen and a colleague, allegedly also American, were held upon their arrival on a UN aircraft from Djibouti. In September, two Americans who had been held hostage by the Houthis for months were freed and flown to safety in Oman, along with a British citizen and three Saudis. The Houthis, who overthrew Yemen's government from Sanaa this year, are currently facing an air and ground campaign by a multinational coalition led by Saudi Arabia and supported by the U.S. Oman, which is not part of the coalition, has been actively involved in negotiations aimed at ending the conflict. The conflict has resulted in at least 5,700 deaths, with around half being civilians, according to the UN, since the end of March.

Koukash's sports club was penalized with a six-point deduction and a £5,000 fine in 2014 and 2015 by the RFL for violating the salary cap. Prior to this ruling, he threatened to wage an open war against the RFL if they were found guilty. "I am in negotiations with several chairmen to arrange a meeting to express a vote of no confidence in the RFL's leadership," said Koukash. "They are not competent for their roles. We invest vast sums into rugby league and aim for the sport's betterment. "I have been involved in the sport for four years, and during this time, I observe that the game has taken a commercial step backward. "Millionaire racehorse owner Koukash would require six of the 12 Super League clubs to call an urgent meeting and propose a no-confidence motion. In response, the RFL issued a statement: "Our purpose is to serve the clubs and all those passionate about rugby league. Our governance provides a well-established democratic process that allows clubs to voice their concerns, and we always listen to their opinions. "Although we will persist in our efforts to enhance the fortunes of all clubs, a recent independent benchmarking report indicates that, as a sport, we are financially healthier than we were two years ago." Koukash will address the media on Wednesday, 18 May, where he is expected to address the recent salary cap charges in more detail.
The speaker has exclusively interacted with the company's executives and stock market investors regarding economic changes. They anticipate that their understanding of the economic landscape may evolve as they engage with other parties. However, there is a sense of relief among these individuals that the US Federal Reserve has postponed the end of the era of historically low interest rates on dollar-denominated debts, a policy instituted following the 2008 financial crisis. The Fed's decision to delay a rate hike is not solely due to concerns for Chinese stock market speculators and businesses. The Fed chairman has explicitly stated that interest rates would have been increased if not for concerns over unstable market and economic conditions outside the US, particularly the uncertain pace of China's economic growth and its impact on emerging economies, particularly commodity producers and manufacturers reliant on Chinese demand. In essence, a slowdown in China's growth, which has led to a decline in global economic sentiment and a rise in the value of the US dollar, has already tightened monetary conditions in America. This, in turn, has made American investors feel less prosperous and has made it more difficult for American exporters to generate sales. Chairman Yellen's stance is that this indirect and modest impact of China's slowdown on US prosperity is comparable to the impact of a small interest rate hike she would have announced. If inflation is a concern in the US, which is a matter of debate, then China's slowdown has lessened that risk by moderating America's recovery. However, this analysis raises two concerns. First, investors may worry that if even the Fed is cautious about China, the economic slowdown there could be more severe than anticipated. This could exacerbate market volatility. Second, the prolonged period of artificially low interest rates has inflated a global debt bubble. The longer it takes for rates to rise again, even gradually, the greater the apprehension that this bubble will eventually burst with a catastrophic and painful impact, rather than a smooth deflation.

With a new head coach now needed, Ray McKinnon of Raith Rovers has emerged as a front-runner for the position. After confirming his departure, Paatelainen expressed gratitude to the players, staff, and supporters, acknowledging the challenges faced during a difficult winter. Having taken over from Jackie McNamara in October, Paatelainen had been unable to prevent a decline in United's fortunes, overseeing only five wins in 25 Premiership matches before their relegation was confirmed following a 2-1 loss to city rivals Dundee. Thompson expressed regret to the fans, pledging changes to hasten United's return to the top division. The team's next match is against Inverness Caledonian Thistle on Friday. Despite Dundee United expressing interest in McKinnon, Raith Rovers have made it clear they will not entertain any approaches for their manager while they remain in the Premiership play-offs. Raith Rovers are set to face Hibernian in the first leg of their play-off quarter-final on Wednesday. Eric Drysdale, a director at Raith Rovers, has stated that they have received no contact from Dundee United or any other club regarding McKinnon, and any such contact would be unwelcome at this time.
In 1987, Daniel Morgan was tragically found dead in a car park adjacent to a London pub, the Golden Lion in Sydenham, following an axe attack. Despite five separate police investigations, no one has ever been successfully prosecuted for his murder. Alastair Morgan, Daniel's brother, has teamed up with investigative journalist Peter Jukes to share the harrowing story of Daniel's murder in a series of weekly installments. Alastair expressed his desire for the public to hear the truth, stating that the story has never been coherently and logically presented before. He believes the case, which has been marred by allegations of police corruption and cover-ups, is a shocking one that deserves attention. When Daniel's body was discovered in March 1987, he had recently departed from the Golden Lion pub. Various police investigations repeatedly failed to secure a conviction, and the case has been plagued with claims of misconduct and suppression of evidence. An independent panel has been established to scrutinize the circumstances surrounding Daniel's death and the ongoing police inability to secure a conviction. Daniel, a resident of Llanfrechfa near Cwmbran, was only 37 years old at the time of his death. Peter Jukes, the journalist spearheading the new podcast, was astounded by the details of the case as he delved into his research. He hopes that witnesses will come forward with new information that could help shed light on the events. With the abundance of open-source material available, the public can piece together the story for themselves and potentially uncover new connections. During the recording process, Alastair revisited the scene of his brother's murder with the podcast's production team. Peter Jukes praises the podcast format as an effective means of presenting complex, in-depth stories. He notes the flexibility of the medium, as it allows for movement and reliance on a single voice, such as a presenter or, in this case, a brother of a murder victim. The producers aim to replicate the success of the Serial podcast, which tells a single true story over the course of a series. The first series generated questions about the conviction of an American man for murdering his high school girlfriend. The Daniel Morgan Murder podcast is scheduled to be released exclusively to registered subscribers
The Elmbridge Museum announced its "museum without walls" initiative, aiming to deliver its services in a more accessible, relevant, and cost-effective manner. The physical gallery in Weybridge closed its doors on Saturday, and the museum's new website went live on Sunday. It was noted that Surrey County Council owns the museum building, and a decision regarding its future is pending. The borough council highlighted that the new website offers an engaging interactive online experience, representing the museum as a whole and showcasing its various services. A dedicated "object in focus" section provides in-depth information on select objects, while the "what we're up to" section offers insights into projects undertaken by the museum team, now based at the Civic Centre in Esher. While the museum's physical objects will still be displayed at temporary exhibitions throughout the borough, it will also run a schools program in September. Currently, two exhibitions are on display at Thames Ditton Library and Walton Library. The museum's collection is being transferred to a purpose-built storage facility, where appointments can be made to view the artefacts.
Scarborough Hospital, facing financial and care quality challenges, has expressed interest in partnering with York Hospital due to the government's mandate for all hospitals to become foundation trusts by 2013. Scarborough Hospital's financial struggles, including debts of £4m, and recent criticism from regulators for subpar care, have made it unlikely to meet the criteria for independent foundation trust status. The hospital's board acknowledges that achieving this goal within three years is impossible without assistance. York Hospital, which obtained foundation status in 2007, has been identified as the preferred partner. A spokesperson for the Scarborough and North East Yorkshire NHS Trust stated, "To become a foundation trust, hospital trusts must meet specific clinical and financial standards that ensure a sustainable future. The requirement to achieve foundation trust status by 2013 places us in a difficult position as we are unlikely to meet the criteria to operate independently. Lack of foundation trust status would impede our ability to guarantee clinical services and staffing across all our sites." At its meeting on Tuesday, the board discussed various future options to secure clinically and financially sustainable services for Scarborough and the surrounding areas, given the challenging financial climate and evolving health policy. The board has decided to approach the York Hospital Foundation Trust to explore potential partnership opportunities. Patrick Crowley, CEO of York Teaching Hospital NHS Foundation Trust, commented, "To become a foundation trust, hospital trusts must meet specific clinical and financial standards that ensure a sustainable future as an independent organization within the NHS. We have been collaborating closely with NHS Yorkshire and the Humber and other health partners over the past few months to determine how this can be achieved for Scarborough." Mr. Crowley added that the York trust had not yet formally responded to the approach by the Scarborough board, but all partners are optimistic about continuing existing alliances and partnerships to deliver healthcare services for the population.
The letter, signed by Angela Constance, the Scottish Secretary for Equalities, and Carl Sargeant, her Welsh counterpart, expresses concern over the lack of planning and communication in the implementation of the Dubs resettlement scheme for unaccompanied child refugees. Despite the UK government's pledge to accept up to 480 children under the scheme, only approximately 200 have been transferred thus far, with no arrivals in 2017, as confirmed by the Home Office last week. The Dubs amendment, named after Labour peer Lord Dubs, a child refugee who came to the UK before World War Two, requires the UK government to offer assistance to a specified number of unaccompanied child refugees arriving in Europe without family connections. However, the letter criticizes the insufficient sharing of valuable information and planning, which has hampered the ability to effectively plan ahead. Immigration Minister Brandon Lewis acknowledged the UK government's commitment to fulfilling its obligations under the Dubs scheme as soon as possible, while also emphasizing other mechanisms for assisting vulnerable children. He pointed out that the UK has committed to resettling 23,000 people directly from conflict zones and granted protection or another form of leave to over 8,000 children in the previous year. The Minister also emphasized that the most vulnerable children are in the conflict zone around Syria, and the best way to help them is by resettling refugees directly from the region, thus preventing traffickers and smugglers from exploiting vulnerable people and children. The Minister expressed gratitude for the support provided by Scotland and Wales and announced the intention to extend the National Transfer Scheme to the rest of the UK, allowing local authorities to fully participate.
The Scottish Environment Protection Agency (SEPA) has accused Dawnfresh of excessively using the organophosphorus pesticide azamethiphos at one of its sites in Loch Etive. This pesticide is utilized to combat parasites like sea lice. Dawnfresh acknowledged a "very small number of errors" had occurred. As one of the UK's largest trout producers, Dawnfresh stated it was collaborating with SEPA to minimize future environmental impact at the farm. The breach of regulations was reported to SEPA by the conservation charity Friends of Loch Etive. Last year, Dawnfresh produced approximately 3,000 tonnes of rainbow trout at Loch Etive. A SEPA spokesperson explained that the agency was investigating instances where consecutive azamethiphos treatments were carried out at the Etive 6 site less than 24 hours after the first treatment, which violates the site's Controlled Activities Regulations (CAR) license. Stewart Hawthorn, Dawnfresh Farming director, revealed that the company had recorded a historically low number of sea lice in Loch Etive the previous year due to a more proactive approach to the problem. However, he admitted that there were six instances where the company did not meet its usual high standards in the technical implementation of a treatment on one of its sites. Hawthorn expressed frustration that these errors resulted in the site not receiving an 'excellent' rating in environmental compliance from SEPA. He assured that Dawnfresh would work with SEPA and its own team to ensure a lower environmental impact in the future. Hawthorn also expressed pride in Dawnfresh's record of environmental compliance, with three other operating sites on Loch Etive receiving ratings of 'excellent' (twice) and 'good' (once). He mentioned that two further sites would not be operated again because Dawnfresh felt it could not do so while maintaining the highest standards of environmental protection. Looking ahead to 2017, Hawthorn stated that Dawnfresh remained committed to effectively controlling sea lice and was already implementing new treatment methods to further reduce reliance on chemicals.

The team at Claythorpe Watermill, situated close to Alford, Lincolnshire, has expressed concerns about Stan, their resident cockerel. Known for his tendency to chase toddlers and peck ankles, they believe that with the impending busy summer season, it would be more suitable for Stan to find a new living arrangement. Owner Rebecca Agate expressed her desire for visitors to have an uninterrupted, enjoyable experience at the watermill, stating, "We have a high influx of small children visiting the park, and if Stan is chasing or pecking, he can be quite intimidating. To prevent visitors from recalling their visit negatively, we are seeking a new home for him." Agate described Stan, who is believed to be part Dutch bantam, as having a vibrant personality and enjoying human company. However, she also mentioned that he can exhibit a grumpy demeanor. Historically, there have been numerous instances of birds exhibiting aggressive behavior towards people, animals, or objects. For example, in Cambridgeshire last year, a pheasant was labeled a "terrorist" for attacking vehicles, chasing pets, and trapping a delivery driver for 20 minutes by blocking his path, attacking the bonnet, and chasing his van. Another case involved a pheasant named Phil attacking members of a Shropshire family, forcing one of them to carry a badminton racket for self-defense. Claythorpe Watermill and Wildfowl Gardens houses a variety of animals, including waterfowl, wallabies, chipmunks, peacocks, and a family of otters.
Approximately 20,000 Syrian refugees are anticipated to be resettled in the UK over the subsequent five years. Discussions have arisen regarding housing, education, and healthcare, as well as the funding for additional services. The Local Government Association has advocated for additional resources to aid its members in housing these individuals, rather than depleting their own limited housing stock. BBC correspondent Daniel Sandford stated that the UK aims to accept around 400 refugees monthly, selected by the United Nations Refugee Agency (UNHCR). The plan is to initiate resettlement from October. Sandford added that many local authorities are reluctant to utilize their own council housing stock, instead trying to find landlords willing to house Syrian refugees, with the costs covered by the state. Prime Minister David Cameron confirmed that these individuals will come from camps bordering Syria, rather than those already in Europe. Unlike other asylum seekers, they will be permitted to commence work immediately and will be eligible for benefits. David Simmons from the Local Government Association expressed the desire for councils to receive reassurance that long-term plans are in place to support these individuals. "This is not merely about short-term funding, but ensuring that resources are available so that families and children are adequately supported," he said. "They need to be able to assimilate into life in the UK, considering their education, employment, and housing prospects." Meanwhile, ministers from Central Europe have again refused a mandatory quota system for distributing migrant arrivals. In recent weeks, tens of thousands of migrants have been attempting to reach Europe from war-torn Syria and Libya. Many have traversed Hungary en route to Germany, Austria, and Sweden - wealthier EU nations with more lenient asylum laws. European Council President Donald Tusk has announced his intention to convene an emergency summit later this month if a resolution to the crisis is not found promptly.

The Purchasing Managers Index (PMI) of the country decreased to 50.8 from the previous month's 51.1, falling below the anticipated increase in growth pace. A score above 50 indicates expansion. Analysts had predicted a slight uptick in growth. Recently disclosed data indicated the broader Chinese economy expanding at its slowest rate in over five years, with growth between July and September at 7.3%, down from 7.5% in the previous quarter. Following the release of the PMI data on Saturday, analysts at China International Capital stated, "There remains pressure on the economy, and monetary policy will remain accommodative." In response to this slowdown, Beijing has announced measures to stimulate consumer spending, such as loosening home purchase restrictions and injecting billions of dollars into the country's largest banks. The Chinese central bank has also reduced certain inter-bank interest rates. The government aims to attain 7.5% economic growth this year, but many analysts are skeptical about meeting this target. Speculation exists that additional measures may be taken to boost growth. Such high rates of growth are essential to create enough jobs for China's vast and increasingly educated population. However, China's growth objectives are significantly higher than the expected rates in more developed economies - the latest figures show the US economy growing at a 3.5% annual rate.
David Tinsley, an economist based in the UK for UBS, stated that Brexit would lead to significantly decreased growth, a substantial depreciation of the pound, and additional monetary easing from the Bank of England. He anticipates the central bank to implement two interest rate reductions over the following six months, bringing rates down from their current record low of 0.5% to zero. Interest rates have been at 0.5% since 2009 as Britain has struggled to recuperate from the 2008 financial crisis. UBS also predicts that the vote will delay interest rate increases in the US. Initially, economists believed that Janet Yellen, the governor of the US central bank, the Federal Reserve, would raise rates in September; however, UBS now believes this will not occur. Mr. Tinsley expects the UK's growth rates to decline to zero in the latter half of the year, as the economy had previously been growing at approximately 2%. In the long term, there could be even more extensive damage. The outcome heavily depends on future trade negotiations and the type of access the UK has to the European single market. In his opinion, Brexit could potentially reduce the UK's long-term GDP by approximately 3.0% under a scenario in which access is significantly restricted.
At the age of 84, Harry Gregg, a native of Northern Ireland, lived through the 1958 Munich air disaster that claimed the lives of 23 individuals, among whom were eight of his teammates from Manchester United. Reflecting on the event, Gregg shared, "When the news broke, I asked my wife if I could be alone in the television room. I didn't want anyone with me. I didn't know how to react. It's extremely difficult to describe." Recently, Gregg was reached out by a distraught Brazilian journalist following the tragedy in Colombia that occurred on Monday, claiming 71 lives, including 19 players from Chapecoense, en route to play in one of South America's major competitions' finals. Gregg recollected, "At Munich, I lost my friends and fellow players, but there were others on board, including one of the country's greatest journalists at the time." Upon sharing this with the Brazilian journalist, he expressed his gratitude, saying, "Harry Gregg, I am so relieved that you remember everyone who died on the plane because I lost three friends on that aircraft who were sports journalists." Gregg emphasized, "As with Munich, the focus might be on the lost players, but we should never forget the others who died. I hope that gave this Brazilian journalist some comfort, as he too was grieving." In Munich, Gregg bravely stayed with the burning plane post the air crash and saved several lives, including a mother and her baby. Six individuals, including three players, managed to survive Monday's crash near Medellin, Colombia, although goalkeeper Jackson Follmann has had to undergo amputation of his right leg. Gregg attributes his return to the training field following the accident as what prevented him from succumbing to the insanity of the situation. A few months after the Munich air disaster, Gregg was recognized as the best goalkeeper in the world in acknowledgment of his exceptional performances for Northern Ireland during the 1958 World Cup held in Sweden.
Journalist Rafael Marques de Morais has been accused of defaming seven Angolan generals, who are allegedly connected to acts of murder, torture, and land theft in the country's diamond mines. Reports suggest that several individuals were arrested for protesting the trial. De Morais is a well-known critic of President Jose Eduardo dos Santos' three-and-a-half-decade rule in Angola. In 1999, he was imprisoned for 43 days, 11 of which were spent in solitary confinement, following the publication of an article titled "The Lipstick of the Dictatorship" in a private Angolan newspaper. Criticism in Angola is often met with intolerance, with some critics either bribed, jailed, or disappeared, according to BBC Africa analyst Mary Harper. The latest charges against de Morais follow the publication of his book, "Blood Diamonds: Torture and Corruption in Angola." One of the generals' lawyers, Joao Manuel, has stated that there is no connection between the Angolan military and the crimes exposed. The trial, set to take place in Luanda, will be held in secret, according to Judge Adriano Cerveira. Outside the courtroom, skirmishes erupted between police and protesters who chanted "free Rafael" and "imprison the generals." After the case was adjourned until April 23, de Morais stated, "I faced nine charges of criminal defamation today, but I leave with an additional 15 charges." De Morais recently received a freedom of expression award in the UK from the campaign group Index on Censorship, which called for the charges against him to be dropped. Prior to the trial, de Morais told the BBC's Focus on Africa radio program that Angola's leaders live extravagant lives with luxury homes and cars, yet denounce critics as "stooges of imperialists" when they demand freedoms enjoyed in the West. If convicted, de Morais could face up to nine years in prison and a fine of $1.2 million. The unregulated diamond trade was instrumental in fueling Angola's 27-year civil war, which ended in 2002. Since the end of the conflict, Angola, one of Africa's major oil producers, has experienced economic growth

In 1973, John Cleese drew inspiration for his TV sitcom, Fawlty Towers, from the Gleneagles Hotel in Torquay, having stayed there with the Monty Python team. Churchill Retirement Living will repurpose the site, following Torbay Council's approval of their plans. Unbeknownst to him, the former owner, Donald Sinclair, unwittingly served as the model for Cleese's character, Basil Fawlty. The hotel, boasting 41 bedrooms, closed its doors earlier this year, and Churchill Retirement Living submitted an application for 36 retirement apartments on the site. Initially, Torbay Council's development management committee rejected the proposal, expressing concerns about its size and perceived insensitivity to the area. However, a scaled-down, revised scheme was subsequently accepted. This revised plan includes demolishing the three-star hotel and constructing 21 one-bedroom and 11 two-bedroom apartments, complete with a guest suite and two communal lounges. The planning officers permitted the conversion of the site from tourist accommodation to residential, as they determined the former hotel to be commercially unviable. Fawlty Towers, ranked as the number one television program by the British Film Institute in 2000, aired only 12 episodes.

Each year, 70 individuals lose their lives, and hundreds of thousands sustain injuries, due to fires originating in cookers, refrigerators, and tumble dryers. The Electrical Safety Council (ESC) emphasizes that manufacturers must take more proactive steps to identify and contact customers when safety concerns arise. They argue that the existing guidelines are inadequate. In December, Catherine Paterson, a resident of Middlesbrough, experienced a fire that devastated her garage. The fire was traced back to her four-month-old tumble dryer. After investigating online, she discovered that the specific model she was using had been recalled due to safety issues by the manufacturer. "Approximately ten minutes after the drier was turned on, we received a call from our neighbor, informing us that our garage was on fire," she shared with the BBC. The fire was so intense that it destroyed the garage within fifteen minutes, causing approximately £10,000 in damage. "They were aware of the product's fault since the end of November, but no one reached out to us," Catherine lamented. It wasn't until early February that someone finally contacted them about the issue, which was two months after the fire. According to Trading Standards, the tumble dryer's manufacturer took necessary steps to inform the public about the faulty product, including media and online notices. However, Steven Curtler, product safety manager at the Electrical Safety Council (ESC), contends that Catherine's case underscores the inadequacy of the current guidelines for manufacturers. He is now advocating for changes in industry practices to prioritize consumer safety. "One area we believe could see significant improvement is product traceability," he stated. The ESC suggests that more consumer information should be collected at the time of purchase to facilitate the dissemination of critical safety information. According to data from the ESC, an average of 70 lives are lost and 350,000 individuals are seriously injured annually due to household appliances such as refrigerator-freezers, gas cookers, and washing machines. In 2011, a tragic incident occurred in north London, where a fridge-freezer caused the death of a mother and her five children. The London Fire Brigade reported that fridge-freezers are the most hazardous household appliance when involved in a fire. The issue

On a Wednesday, a Mumbai court convicted actor Khan for a five-year prison sentence in the fatal hit-and-run incident involving Noor Ullah Khan. The Bombay High Court granted Khan interim bail for two days after his lawyers filed an appeal against his sentence. Noor Ullah Khan, aged 38, was one of five individuals struck in the accident; three sustained serious injuries, and another person received minor injuries when Khan's Toyota Land Cruiser collided with an American Express bakery in Bandra, Mumbai, late on September 28, 2002. Despite Khan's consistent claims that his driver was driving, the judge determined that the actor himself was driving under the influence of alcohol. Following his interim bail, Khan – who faced a potential 10-year jail term – returned to his home, where several Bollywood stars paid him a visit. Reports indicate that Khan is not required to appear in court on Friday for his bail hearing. This case has captivated both Bollywood and India for years. Judge DW Deshpande, who found him guilty of culpable homicide, stated in his 240-page ruling that Khan "failed to visit the hospital to meet the injured or provide aid." He added that Khan "could have immediately reported to the police if he was innocent."

The Queen Street Mill Museum in Burnley, one of five museums owned by Lancashire County Council, is set to close, although it will remain open for school visits. This decision also applies to Helmshore Mills Museum, the last working example of Lancashire cotton spinning and weaving. The council aims to save £65m by 2018, leading to this tough decision. Councillor Marcus Johnstone, responsible for environment, planning, and cultural services, stated, "Closing museums is our last resort, but the severity of Lancashire County Council's financial predicament necessitates such hard choices to protect essential services for our community's most vulnerable individuals." In addition to the Museum of Lancashire in Preston and Fleetwood's Maritime Museum, Judges' Lodgings in Lancaster will also close. Initially, the council planned to close these five museums in the spring, but the schedule has been delayed to facilitate discussions with potential operators. A council representative confirmed that these discussions are still ongoing. Over 10,000 signatures were gathered on a petition to save the museums at Queen Street and Helmshore Mills, describing them as "a vital pillar of Lancashire's substantial industrial legacy" during the county's significant role in Britain's Industrial Revolution.
The Foster for Fife Choir is performing a composition penned exclusively for them by Fife composer Ian Hammond Brown, titled "Help a Child Belong." This piece carries a powerful message, encouraging individuals to offer a home to a child during a challenging period in their lives. The choir has been gracing stages in community halls and shopping centers across Fife. It is projected that approximately 800 foster families are required in Scotland within the next year to meet the demand. Rae Ormiston, from Fife Council's children and families department, stated, "We are persistently seeking innovative methods to recruit foster carers and bring fostering to the attention of the general public, and that's precisely what the choir is accomplishing." She further added, "Throughout Scotland, we've observed a decrease in individuals coming forward. We've noticed a slowdown in numbers, which is why we must promote our need more frequently." Nikki Perry, a member of the Foster for Fife Choir and a foster mother for over a hundred children in her seventeen years, expressed hope that the choir would highlight to prospective caregivers the immense rewards associated with this role. She stated, "It's an enriching experience for everyone involved, witnessing children grow, move on, and establish their own families, potentially for the first time. If I had a larger home, I'd take in another twenty children. Unfortunately, I don't, and we certainly need more foster carers in Fife." Nine-year-old choir member Brooklyn shared his experiences of finding a foster family. He said, "I enjoy having a place to call home and a family to care for me. They are always kind to me." The Foster for Fife Choir is believed to be the first of its kind in Scotland.
In 2016, the global number of ultra-high-net-worth individuals, defined as those with over $30 million in net assets, increased by 6,340 to reach 193,490, according to property consultants Knight Frank. This rise followed a decline in the previous year. Researchers attribute the turnaround to robust performances on global stock markets. Despite political surprises and economic uncertainties, such as the UK's Brexit vote and the election of Donald Trump, many developed economies still showed strong growth. Stock markets in the US and UK even reached record highs towards the end of the year. Andrew Amoils, head of research at New World Wealth, the research company that provided the data for the report, commented, "There may be widespread uncertainty, but there are also strong fundamentals in many economies, with signs of real progress being made around regulation and policy which will help economic growth to flourish in some places." Knight Frank predicts that the number of ultra-high-net-worth individuals worldwide will grow by 43% over the next decade. However, they anticipate wide variations between regions and countries. The US is expected to see slightly more growth than the UK, but the rest of Europe will only see 12% growth. In contrast, Asia is projected to experience the biggest rise, with a 91% increase anticipated. By 2026, Asia is expected to have almost caught up with the US, with only 7,068 fewer super-rich individuals. Currently, the US leads by 27,020. Asian cities, such as Singapore, Shanghai, and Beijing, are predicted to surpass current wealth concentrations, like that of San Francisco, as their wealthy populations grow. Several African countries, including Ethiopia, Rwanda, and Tanzania, are also expected to see significant increases in their wealthy populations.

Middle-aged Scots, aged 45 to 54, reportedly spend an average of 7.8 hours daily engaged in sedentary activities, such as work, eating, or screen time. This is more than the over-75s, who spend 7.4 hours daily in such activities. These findings come from a study conducted by researchers at the University of Edinburgh's Physical Activity for Health Research Centre and are published in the Journal of Sports Sciences. The study utilized data from over 14,000 individuals in Scotland, gathered from the 2012-14 Scottish Health Survey. Conversely, at the weekend, the over-75s are the least sedentary, spending between 7.3 and 7.4 hours daily sitting, while those aged 25 to 54 are the least sedentary, with daily sedentary time ranging from 5.2 to 5.7 hours. The youngest group, 16 to 24-year-olds, is less sedentary than the over-75s during weekdays. The majority of the time spent sitting for the youngest group is in front of a television or screen. Men tend to spend less time in front of screens as they age, with women peaking in middle-age. Lead researcher Tessa Strain stated, "Large parts of the population are dangerously sedentary, something we have underestimated. We need to tackle high levels of sedentary time in early and middle age, when patterns may develop. Our findings suggest that changing habits in the workplace could be an appropriate place to start, given how much time we spend sitting there every day." Excessive sedentary time, more than seven hours a day, is associated with an increased risk of early death, cardiovascular disease, type 2 diabetes, and certain cancers, even if individuals are physically active at other times of the day.

China regards the island as a renegade province, and has previously threatened military action if necessary to reclaim it. Prior to her election, Ms. Tsai expressed a desire to maintain the "status quo." Ocado's warehouse in Andover, Hampshire, is equipped with automated systems where robots select crates containing specific items for customer orders. While these crates are currently handed over to a human team for final selection, the company is considering replacing them with robotic hands in the future. Additionally, Ocado is developing a humanoid maintenance robot called SecondHands, designed to work alongside human colleagues in maintaining the warehouse. The Soma project, a five-year research collaboration between five European universities and Disney, is developing a fruit and vegetable picker robot. According to Ocado spokesman Alexandru Voica, the demonstration device is an early prototype. The goal is to mimic the human hand's flexibility and adaptability by creating a gripper based on air pressure that controls the movement of the robotic fingers. The robot's development includes combining computer vision, allowing it to recognize products by looking at them, with the gripping aspect. At present, only the gripper is being demonstrated, but the robot will eventually learn to distinguish fruit ripeness through machine learning. It will also be capable of picking other items, such as wine bottles and detergent, which require different care. Mr. Voica noted that fruit and vegetables are the most challenging items to pick. He stated, "When the customer gets their bag of bananas or tomatoes, if they see the product is damaged, they don't care whether it's a human or a robot that picked it." Prof. Chris Melhuish, director of the Bristol Robotics Laboratory, explained that building robotic devices to carry out multiple tasks is challenging. He noted that understanding and exploiting the way the human hand functions, due to its flexibility and adaptability, makes sense. While there are numerous groups working on robotic manipulation, often for specific purposes, the goal is to create a general-purpose manipulator that can perform various tasks.
The club has secured a Section 106 planning order, allowing them to relocate to their new stadium at Silver Bow on the city's outskirts by July 26, 2017. According to Truro chairman Peter Masters, construction will commence as early as October this year. The arrangement is reminiscent of the one awaiting the developers of the Stadium for Cornwall, who are hoping to initiate development of their 10,000-seat stadium for the rugby union club Cornish Pirates. Both grounds received planning approval in July 2015, but had to await approval from the Department of Local Government and the Section 106 order before commencing development. Originally planning to share Torquay United's Plainmoor ground next season, Truro City FC decided to stay at Treyew Road for one more season. Upon completion of the new stadium, a retail park will be built on the Treyew Road site. The new stadium will meet the minimum 'A' grade standards, with a capacity for 4,000 spectators and the potential to accommodate up to 5,000, making it suitable for the highest level of non-league football. It will also feature a synthetic 3G surface and conference facilities. Peter Masters and fellow businessman Philip Perryman took over the club in December 2012, when it was on the brink of liquidation, having entered administration earlier that year. After suffering relegation from the Conference South, the club were promoted back to the second tier of non-league football last year, having won the Southern Premier League play-offs. "Considering where we've come from, from £4.5m in debt, the ground being sold to a third party, and relegation, we've managed to turn things around," Masters added. "We'll soon have our own stadium, and after last season's promotion, we aim to make the play-offs this season, all while the club is debt-free."

Prior to the May general election, the Conservative MP for Oxford West and Abingdon, Miss Blackwood, disclosed her diagnosis with Ehlers-Danlos syndrome. This condition impacts the joints and muscles, often causing persistent pain. In her efforts to lessen the societal stigma associated with chronic illnesses, Miss Blackwood has been advocating for increased understanding and acceptance. She was diagnosed with this genetic disorder two years ago, following a period of joint pain, migraines, and asthma. She decided to publicly disclose her illness before the election, believing it was essential to be transparent about her health condition. Additionally, she aimed to demonstrate that individuals with invisible conditions can still excel in demanding, high-profile roles. Miss Blackwood expressed, "I felt it was crucial to clarify that it's not a life-threatening illness, and while it's chronic, it's entirely possible to maintain a regular life and continue with daily activities." She further emphasized that we, as a society, need to overcome the lingering stigma surrounding disability and chronic illness in the UK. During an interview with BBC Oxford, Miss Blackwood shared that she has adapted her diet and taken up Pilates to manage her condition more effectively.

In October 2016, the UK's Communities Secretary, Sajid Javid, gave the green light for shale gas extraction at Cuadrilla's Preston New Road site in Little Plumpton. This decision, according to the Preston New Road Action Group (PNRAG), is fundamentally flawed and an abuse of power. The legal challenge, set for March 15 in Manchester, will contest this ruling. In 2015, Lancashire County Council (LCC) refused permission for shale gas extraction at the site due to concerns about noise and traffic. Cuadrilla appealed this decision, which was subsequently overturned by the Secretary of State, who ruled in favor of Cuadrilla. This decision marks the first time UK shale rock will be fracked horizontally, a method expected to yield more gas. Construction work at the Preston New Road site began in January, and it has since been a focal point for anti-fracking protests. Claire Stephenson of PNRAG criticized Javid's decision, stating it is not a demonstration of democracy but an abuse of power to favor a corporation over the community's wishes. She further argued that the Secretary of State, who is not local and has not been present during any planning inquiries or hearings for the past three years, should not have intervened in favor of Cuadrilla. Both Fylde Borough Council and LCC had previously rejected Cuadrilla's application, with Lancashire voicing a resounding "no." The Department for Communities and Local Government declined to comment on the upcoming case, which will be heard at Manchester's Civil Justice Centre on March 15.

The city council has announced plans to renovate the Robinson Centre in Castlereagh and the Brook Activity Centre in Twinbrook at an estimated cost of £35 million. Additionally, councillors have approved updated plans to convert Windsor House into the Grand Central Hotel, increasing the number of rooms from 200 to 304. The £20 million transformation of the Robinson Centre will involve replacing the existing building with a modern facility, featuring an eight-lane pool and leisure facilities. The centre was closed in 2015 due to health and safety concerns related to asbestos. The £15 million redevelopment of the Brook Activity Centre will focus on outdoor leisure amenities, including a new Gaelic football pitch, two football pitches, and six five-a-side pitches (three indoor and three outdoor). These projects are part of Belfast City Council's £105 million initiative to enhance leisure centres citywide. Cllr Peter Johnston, chair of the council's planning committee, described these redevelopments as an "investment in the future health and well-being of both the city and its citizens." Construction work on both projects is expected to commence over the summer, with facilities becoming operational in early 2019. At a recent planning meeting, approval was also granted for revised plans for Windsor House, Ireland's tallest office block, which was acquired by Hastings Hotels in 2015. The Grand Central Hotel will offer 304 bedrooms, serviced apartments, and office spaces.
Section 18C of Australia's Racial Discrimination Act prohibits individuals from publicly insulting someone based on their race. Senator David Leyonhjelm, a libertarian, advocates for the repeal of this section, arguing that it infringes upon free speech. However, he recently filed a complaint under the same law in an effort to illustrate his point. Columnist Mark Kenny made disparaging remarks about Senator Leyonhjelm in an article, calling him an "angry white male," a "boorish, supercilious know-it-all," and comparing him to a besser block, a type of building block. Leyonhjelm stated that he was not offended by the comments but saw an opportunity to showcase why he believes Section 18C should be repealed. "Under the Act, Mr. Kenny's article is unlawful because it was reasonably likely, given the circumstances, to offend, insult, humiliate, or intimidate another person or a group of people based on their color," he explained in a statement. He further added that the comments were "reasonably likely...to offend or insult some white males." Leyonhjelm anticipates that his complaint will be successful, provided that the Human Rights Commission adjudicators adhere to the law and are not biased. He stated, "If I manage to have Section 18C repealed, Mr. Kenny will be free to insult me as much as he likes." Section 18C stipulates that a person cannot publicly offend, insult, humiliate, or intimidate another person or group based on their race, color, national or ethnic origin. Conservatives have been vocal opponents of the law since it was used to prosecute well-known right-wing commentator Andrew Bolt. Former Prime Minister Tony Abbott expressed his intention to repeal Section 18C in 2013, but later abandoned his efforts due to strong opposition. This week, Abbott rekindled the debate by suggesting that he should have pursued a less extensive reform that excluded the words "offend" and "insult" from the law.
Matthew Chapman, a businessman residing in Louth, Lincolnshire, was the sole occupant of a privately owned helicopter that crashed on June 6th. The inquest revealed that Mr. Chapman, aged 48, had previously dropped off two passengers in the Baldwin Valley before the accident. Coroner John Needham stated that the cause of Mr. Chapman's death remains undetermined. The court was informed that Mr. Chapman departed from Milton Keynes around 06:00 BST, with two passengers on his Bell Jetranger helicopter. Upon arrival at the island, he dropped both passengers off at Creg Ny Baa, a well-known spot for watching the annual TT races. The court also learned that Mr. Chapman planned to refuel at Ronaldsway Airport before rejoining his friends to watch the races. However, his helicopter crashed at approximately 09:00 BST in a field on a hillside near the 33rd milestone on the Mountain Road. Mr. Chapman's body was discovered trapped in the wreckage and was pronounced dead at the scene. A paramedic's report documented "multiple trauma consistent with a helicopter crash." Mr. Needham mentioned that investigations into the crash are being carried out by inspectors from the UK's Air Accidents Investigations Branch (AAIB). The inquest has been postponed to a future, undetermined date.

They have urged the United States Secretary of State, John Kerry, to address concerns over a fair trial during his visit to the UAE this week. Members of the standards committee are questioning whether stricter regulations are necessary for lobbying activities. While Scotland and Westminster have established registers for lobbyists, Wales has yet to follow suit. A campaigner advocates for Wales to implement a lobbying register to promote transparency and avoid potential future scandals. Lobbyists, who are typically companies or individuals hired to influence government decisions, have been a source of concern due to their covert nature. Plaid Cymru AM Neil McEvoy previously called for lobbying in Wales to be regulated and for lobbyists to be required to register during an assembly debate. He argued that such regulation would foster a transparent culture, making it clear who commercial lobbyists represent. However, the outgoing standards commissioner, Mr Elias, told the committee that there have been no complaints about lobbying at the National Assembly. Despite this, the need for a statutory register of lobbyists was discussed, with concerns about significant resource implications. Tamasin Cave, head of the Alliance for Lobbying Transparency, emphasized the importance of knowing who is influencing government decisions and what deals are being made. She suggested a lobbying register as a means of achieving this transparency, requiring paid lobbyists to disclose their clients, the government officials they are lobbying, and the issues they are seeking to influence. Huw Roberts, chairman of Deryn, a prominent Welsh lobbying company, stated that his company publishes a list of clients and adheres to a strong code of conduct as members of the Association of Professional Political Consultants (APPC). The chairman of the APPC, Mark Glover, underscored the importance of ensuring any new Welsh register provides consistent levels of transparency for both consultant and in-house lobbyists, without being overly bureaucratic or costly. In 2013, the assembly standards committee recommended that AMs face tighter scrutiny but not a full official register. The First Minister, Carwyn Jones, has stated that lobbyists do not have access to Welsh ministers. Assembly members on the committee have agreed to conduct a written consultation on the issue at their meeting on Tuesday.
The Vatican City, nestled within the Italian capital Rome, is home to a diverse community of priests and nuns from various nations. Historically, it represents a minuscule remnant of the vast Papal States that once spanned central Italy, seized by the Italian unification forces in the mid-19th century. For over half a century, popes were effectively "imprisoned" within the Apostolic Palace, reluctant to leave until the Lateran Treaty of 1929 was negotiated by Italy's Fascist government, establishing the present-day micro-state. Within its modest 0.44 square kilometers, the Vatican City boasts numerous imposing structures, such as St Peter's Basilica, a renowned pilgrimage site, and the Vatican Museums and Art Galleries, which house the valuable art collections amassed by the popes. In response to international demands for financial transparency, the Vatican has taken steps to address concerns following an investigation into the Vatican Bank for breaches of money-laundering regulations in 2010. The Vatican's official languages are Latin and Italian, while Christianity is the predominant religion. The life expectancy for men is 74 years and 81 years for women. The euro is the currency, and the Pope serves as the head of state. In March 2013, the College of Cardinals elected Cardinal Archbishop Jorge Mario Bergoglio of Buenos Aires, making him the first Latin American pope, succeeding Pope Benedict XVI, who had resigned due to ill-health after an eight-year reign. Despite being two years older than Benedict at the time of his election, Bergoglio, known as Pope Francis, defied expectations by not being the younger candidate chosen to lead the Catholic Church through its numerous challenges. He is conservative on homosexuality but liberal on social issues such as poverty and inequality. Vatican Radio, or "The Pope's Voice," broadcasts powerful transmissions to a global audience, although it has faced allegations that its transmissions have put lives at risk in a Rome suburb due to exceeding Italy's electromagnetic radiation standards. These claims have been denied by the Vatican. The papacy maintains an active Twitter account, @pont

The president's critics argue that his bid for a third term contravenes the constitution, which requires him to step down after two terms. Last week, Scott Van Zyl was tragically killed on the banks of the Limpopo river, according to Sakkie Louwrens, the director of a South African crime-fighting NGO. Louwrens stated that Van Zyl went missing during a hunting safari last week. His death marks the latest in a series of fatal crocodile attacks in Zimbabwe. Louwrens spoke to the BBC, revealing that Van Zyl embarked on a hunting trip on the Zimbabwe-South Africa border with a local tracker and a pack of dogs. The pair reportedly left their vehicle and separated to search for crocodiles. A search and rescue operation was initiated when Van Zyl's dogs returned to their camp without him. His footprints were found near the river bank, leading to his discarded backpack. Van Zyl was a married man with two children and was known for taking foreign clients on hunting trips. Louwrens explained that staff from the Heritage Protection Group, an organization he heads to assist South African police in combating crime, informally aided the Zimbabwean authorities in their search. "Permission was granted to shoot three Nile crocodiles in the area, and one of them contained Van Zyl's remains," he said. "Subsequent DNA tests confirmed the remains to be those of Van Zyl." At least four fatal crocodile attacks have been reported in Zimbabwe this year. One conservation group, One Green Planet, has criticized the circumstances surrounding his "unnecessary" death. "He should not have been hunting in the first place. Animals in the wild... are wild! They are living, thinking beings with instincts for survival," the group stated.

In March 2015, the tugboat Asterix was maneuvering the chemical tanker Donizetti away from a dock at the Fawley marine terminal when it suddenly tilted sideways and capsized. The coxswain was trapped in the wheelhouse, but was rescued by a colleague just before the vessel sank. The Marine Accident Investigation Branch (MAIB) discovered several safety issues during their investigation. The coxswain was reportedly not adequately trained in the proper use of a specific rope, known as a 'gog', which is employed to prevent a tug from being pulled over sideways. The investigation also uncovered deficiencies in the communication between the Donizetti and Asterix. Additionally, the report noted that the launch crews were not sufficiently proficient in operating the tug's towing hook emergency release mechanism. As a result of the incident, safety and training recommendations have been made to Østensjø Rederi AS, ABP Southampton, and the National Workboat Association. A crew member of the tugboat was later honored with a bravery award for his role in rescuing the coxswain. Both men required hospital treatment for shock and hypothermia.

The Council of Mortgage Lenders (CML) has announced a significant decrease in mortgage loan demand during April, with £18.4bn worth of mortgages advanced, marking an 11% drop compared to March. Despite this decline, the CML noted that monthly mortgage lending figures can be volatile, and a decrease in activity is common during the spring. Adjusting for seasonal factors, the CML stated that the amount borrowed last month was higher than the average for the past year, and was 4% higher than in April 2016. CML's senior economist, Mohammad Jamei, commented, "The housing market appears to be, in essence, maintaining its position." However, other indicators suggest a slowdown in the housing market. For instance, HM Revenue and Customs reported a 22.5% decrease in property transactions in April compared to March. This decline might be due to landlords accelerating purchases to avoid the latest tax changes, which took effect on April 1st, reducing the amount of tax relief they could claim on mortgage payments. Additionally, the CML revealed that the number of first-time buyers securing mortgages has surpassed the number of home movers for the first time since 1996. The CML's research indicates that while the number of home movers and landlords taking out mortgages is decreasing, the number of first-time buyers is increasing. Jamei added, "First-time buyers and those remortgaging seem to be bolstering the market. Home movers, on the other hand, are experiencing a lull. Their activity has been muted for some time now, and the low number of movers means fewer properties available for sale. This imbalance in supply and demand will continue to support house prices, even as the rate of price increases moderates."

Macsen Oatway, a resident of Neath, is afflicted with LAD1, a scarcely occurring condition that impairs his immune system, with merely 400 individuals worldwide sharing this diagnosis. For several weeks, he resided in a specialized isolation unit, colloquially referred to as a "bubble," in Newcastle. Access to this facility was limited to doctors, nurses, and his parents alone. Macsen underwent a series of blood transfusions, chemotherapy, and a bone marrow treatment. Absent this intervention, he would have been obligated to rely on antibiotics throughout his life. His parents, Richard and Zoe, express that this treatment has drastically improved Macsen's life, and they are advocating for more individuals to register for the bone marrow transplant list. This action would enable other children born with the condition to lead fulfilling lives. Mr. Oatway stated, "The significance of this cannot be overstated. You may never be selected, but if you are granted the chance, seize it with both hands. It's a remarkable opportunity to save a life, and to the anonymous donor who contributed to Macsen, we are deeply grateful." Medical professionals have confirmed that Macsen is now healthy enough to return to school, and his parents note that he enjoys it immensely.

Christopher Langley, hailing from Pontypridd, joined forces with publican James Lovegrove to assemble a collection of paintings. The Campaign for Real Ale (Camra) noted that two pubs close every week in Wales. To date, Mr. Langley has completed 13 paintings, with plans to finish an additional 20 in the coming months, expressing concern over potential history loss. The pubs depicted in his work thus far include The Vulcan, recently rescued by St Fagan's Museum, as well as the York Hotel, the Pantmawr Inn, and the Glendower. Mr. Langley stated, "This project has expanded my understanding. I wasn't raised with an appreciation for pubs, but through my conversations with James about the pubs of Cardiff, I've gained a new perspective on that culture. There is a wealth of history at risk of being lost. This is an opportunity to preserve and share that history." The paintings are created based on sketches or photographs if the buildings no longer exist. Mr. Langley added, "I never truly valued the architectural beauty of pubs before. However, when you stand there and paint them, you recognize the immense effort that went into crafting these spaces."

The Elephant and Castle roundabout in south London was the site of the most accidents involving cyclists between 2009 and 2013, with a total of 80 such incidents. These statistics, analyzed by insurance company Aviva, encompassed cycling accidents within the M25 that were reported to or attended by the police. Transport for London expressed concern, stating, "Any accident on London's roads is one too many." In response, Transport for London announced plans to invest nearly £1bn in upgrading existing Cycle Superhighways, introducing new segregated cycle routes, and overhauling numerous junctions on both their roads and on borough roads. In March 2014, the London mayor's office unveiled a £4bn plan to revamp London's roads, which included a new road layout and more cycle lanes at the Elephant and Castle roundabout. Central London's Trafalgar Square had the second highest number of motor accidents involving cyclists during this period, with 46 incidents recorded over the five-year period. The Liberal Democrat London Assembly Group leader, Caroline Pidgeon, criticized Transport for London, stating, "With such appalling figures as this, it is simply shameful that year after year Transport for London have repeatedly spent just a fraction of their allocated budget on vital improvements to junctions and investing in cycling infrastructure." In 2015, there were four cyclist deaths in London, all involving lorries. The most recent death occurred last week in Victoria, where a mother-of-two was killed. Earlier in February, a three-fold increase in fatalities on the capital's roads led Scotland Yard to reintroduce Operation Safeway. This operation will deploy 600 officers at 166 junctions during morning and evening rush hours for six weeks, targeting road users committing traffic offenses.
Individuals in Scotland can now contact medical advisors by dialing the freephone number 111, instead of the prior 11-digit number. Previously, callers from landlines were charged for a local call, while mobile users often incurred significantly higher charges. This change aligns Scotland with England, where the 111 number has been in use since February. The NHS 24 service, providing advice on non-urgent health issues, will continue to operate 24 hours a day, with nurses and other healthcare professionals available to assist. The announcement of the freephone number was made by Scottish Health Secretary Alex Neil in January of last year, who stated it would eliminate a barrier to healthcare services. This move was supported by poverty campaigners, including Caroline Mockford, who was once charged nearly £8 by her mobile provider for a call to the helpline. She subsequently submitted a petition to the Scottish Parliament, advocating for the elimination of such phone charges.
The Dominican Republic, a vibrant Caribbean nation, is renowned as a significant tourist destination. Alongside its free-trade zones, it has evolved into the country's primary source of employment and revenue, surpassing the traditional reliance on exports such as sugar, coffee, and other commodities. The Dominican Republic is predominantly inhabited by people of mixed European and African descent, reflecting its unique cultural heritage. Western influence is evident in the colonial architecture of its capital, Santo Domingo, as well as in its art and literature. The African influence is palpable in its music. The nation boasts a population of approximately 10.2 million, spread across an area of 48,072 square kilometers (18,696 square miles). Spanish is the major language, and Christianity is the predominant religion. The average life expectancy stands at 71 years for men and 77 years for women. The Dominican peso is the official currency. Danilo Medina Sanchez, an economist and long-standing member of the Dominican Liberation Party (PLD), has been serving as the nation's president since May 2016, following his re-election. He initially assumed office on August 16, 2012, succeeding Leonel Fernandez Reyna, who served as president three times. Media ownership in the Dominican Republic is concentrated in a few economically or politically powerful hands, with numerous terrestrial TV channels, cable TV operators, and radio stations in operation. Press freedom is guaranteed by law, and media outlets express diverse political views. Key historical milestones in the Dominican Republic include: - Christopher Columbus's visit in 1492, when he named the island Hispaniola, or "Little Spain." - The establishment of the first Spanish colony in the Western hemisphere at Santo Domingo in 1496, which later served as the capital of all Spanish colonies in America. - The Treaty of Ryswick in 1697, which gave the western part of the Hispaniola island (Haiti) to France and the eastern part (Santo Domingo - the present Dominican Republic) to Spain. - Spain's cession of its portion of Hispaniola island to France in 1795,
Last month, an investigation was initiated when the PSNI discovered that a law firm illegally obtained confidential documents from a government office. A 69-year-old former investigator for the ombudsman was apprehended in England and later released on bail. The PSNI has announced that an independent police force will take over the investigation. Assistant Chief Constable Stephen Martin told the BBC, "Measures have been implemented to ensure independent guidance has been accessible to the PSNI investigation since its inception. Moreover, we are now actively seeking to engage another police force to independently spearhead the investigation." The new investigation team is expected to be appointed within a few weeks. The decision was made due to concerns about a potential conflict of interest, as the ombudsman is responsible for investigating allegations of misconduct by PSNI officers and former members of the Royal Ulster Constabulary. At least eight former RUC officers are known to have been named in the documents given to the law firm, which are part of an ongoing investigation into police misconduct. The police and security service MI5 believe the material could potentially endanger lives. The police have declined to comment on whether the investigation is limited to documents related to one case being investigated by the ombudsman's office or has been expanded to include other cases. "The PSNI is conducting a criminal investigation into the matter, and it would be inappropriate to comment further," ACC Martin said. The PSNI has temporarily halted the release of sensitive material linked to numerous cases currently being investigated by the ombudsman's office pending a review of security protocols. In addition to the police investigation, the Ombudsman, Dr. Michael Maguire, has referred the alleged theft and unlawful disclosure of documents to the information commissioner. The Centre for the Protection of National Infrastructure has also been requested to perform a review of information handling processes within the ombudsman's office. In a statement, a spokesman for the Police Ombudsman said, "It appears the theft at the heart of this investigation occurred approximately 10 years ago. Even so, we are now looking to bring in the Centre for the Protection of National Infrastructure to carry out a review, which we hope will provide an independent assurance that our current systems for handling material are robust."

Sand artists Remy and Paul Hoggard are utilizing approximately 80 tonnes of sand to craft a sculpture, portraying King John at Runnymede in 1215. The artwork will stand 4 meters (13 feet) tall and span 9 meters (30 feet) wide and is part of the anniversary event, Festival800. Other events, celebrating democracy and freedom, are also being held. Mr. Hoggard, who, alongside his Dutch wife, has created sand sculptures worldwide, stated this project was one of his most daring in terms of size and scale. The artist, originally from Beverley, East Yorkshire, now resides on a farm in Bulgaria. The Magna Carta was a peace treaty between King John and the barons who were in revolt against him and established the principles of law-based freedom. Only three of the 63 clauses in Magna Carta remain in effect. One defends the freedom and rights of the English Church, another pertains to the privileges enjoyed by the City of London, and the third is generally believed to have established the right to trial by jury. One of the four surviving copies of Magna Carta is displayed at Lincoln Castle. Festival 800 takes place from 28 August to 6 September at various locations in Lincoln and includes performances by artists such as Billy Bragg and the Levellers. There will also be comedy, poetry, street theatre, lectures, and debate, according to the organizers.

The Falcon-9 booster successfully touched down on a drone ship off the Florida coast a few minutes after launching a Japanese satellite into orbit. This marks SpaceX's second at-sea landing, having accomplished the feat last month. The achievement is particularly noteworthy as the rocket was traveling at a higher velocity upon return. SpaceX officials have noted that recovering boosters used in geostationary satellite missions is more challenging due to the high velocity required for placement in the appropriate orbit. Upon confirmation of the landing, SpaceX CEO Elon Musk tweeted a humorous comment about needing a larger rocket storage hangar. The primary objective of the latest Falcon launch was to deploy the JCSAT-14 satellite, which will provide telecommunications coverage over the Asia-Pacific region for the Sky Perfect JSAT Corporation. Lift-off took place at 01:21 local time (05:20 GMT) from Florida's Cape Canaveral Air Force Station. The satellite separated from the Falcon's upper-stage, which is not recovered, 32 minutes later. The mission was delayed a day due to poor weather conditions over the Cape. To date, SpaceX has brought back three boosters safely to Earth. Its first successful landing on solid ground occurred in December, near the Florida launch site. However, SpaceX is particularly focused on mastering ocean landings on specialized barges, as many of its missions will necessitate a sea platform as a frequent return location. The high-performance required by the Falcon-9 rocket to send satellites to geostationary transfer orbit means that the booster's speed must be reduced, as well as accounting for the extra loading and heating on components upon return. SpaceX's ultimate goal is to recover, refurbish, and re-fly rockets, which should enable them to offer their customers more affordable launches. The European Commission examined whether tech companies were adhering to a commitment to eradicate hate speech within 24 hours of its reporting. However, the Commission discovered that only 40% of reported instances of hate speech were eliminated within this timeframe. This pledge was made in May, when the companies agreed to a "code of conduct" mediated by the Commission. Justice Commissioner Vera Jourova stated, "The recent weeks and months have demonstrated that social media companies must fulfill their significant role and assume their share of responsibility regarding issues such as online radicalization, illegal hate speech, or false news." The research analyzed 600 instances of hate speech reported to the tech companies during a six-week period in October and November. The monitoring system to assess the tech companies' responsiveness was established in early October. Monitoring groups and NGOs that track racist and fascist movements across Europe utilized the reporting systems on various social media platforms to submit these instances, then monitored the time it took the tech companies to act. Of the 600 reports, 270 were submitted to Facebook, 163 to Twitter, 123 to YouTube, and none to Microsoft. The remaining seven reports were submitted to social media groups that had not endorsed the May pledge. The Commission clarified that the 600 reports were a sample of racist, sexist, and misogynist content and did not encompass all examples of hate speech on the tech companies' platforms during the six-week study period. Approximately 20% of the messages were anti-Muslim, and 23% were anti-Semitic. The tech companies removed the content flagged as hate speech in 169 cases. YouTube removed 48.5% of the content reported to them, Facebook 28.3%, and Twitter 19.1%. The research found that reports were reviewed within 24 hours in 40% of cases, and within 48 hours in a further 43%. Ms Jourova commented, "It is our responsibility to shield people in Europe from online incitement to hatred and violence." She added, "While IT Companies are heading in the right direction, the initial results indicate that the IT companies will need to do more to ensure success."

Carly Fiorina, a woman, and Ben Carson, an African American, have entered the presidential race, marking historic firsts for their respective parties. Both are political outsiders, as opposed to the senators and governors they are now competing against for the nomination. Hillary Clinton, a Democrat, and Jeb Bush, a Republican yet to officially declare his candidacy, are among the frontrunners. Upon her announcement on ABC's Good Morning America, Fiorina criticized Clinton, stating, "I hold Clinton in high regard, but her trustworthiness is questionable, given the recent email server controversy during her tenure as secretary of state." Fiorina lost her only bid for public office, a 2010 Senate race in California, by 10%. Her notable achievement is her tenure as CEO of Hewlett-Packard, a position she lost after six years due to shareholder discontent. Her intentions for running are debated; some argue she seeks publicity rather than votes, given her upcoming book release. Advocates, however, highlight her status as the likely only female Republican candidate this year, with Fortune 500 business experience, and her potential to effectively challenge Democratic frontrunner Hillary Clinton without accusations of sexism. Fiorina has been well-received by Republican audiences prior to her announcement, but it remains to be seen if she can convert these positive feelings into tangible support. However, his controversial views on issues like evolution, healthcare reform, and gay rights have not significantly affected his favorability among core conservative voters. If these voters continue to support Carson next year, he could potentially pose a threat to other socially conservative candidates, such as Texas Senator Ted Cruz and former Arkansas Governor Mike Huckabee.
