The report advocates a shift from existing guidelines that advise prescribing medication only when blood pressure exceeds a specific threshold. Experts recognize the significance of lifestyle factors in lowering blood pressure levels. The study is published in The Lancet. For years, high blood pressure has been associated with a heightened risk of heart disease and stroke. As per the current guidelines, issued by England's National Institute for Health and Care Excellence, medication is recommended for patients when their blood pressure reaches 140 mmHg. Prior to this point, even high-risk individuals, such as those with a history of strokes, are offered monitoring but not medication. Now, a team of international experts is advocating for doctors to focus on an individual's risks instead of rigid and arbitrary blood pressure thresholds. They analyzed the results of over 100 large-scale trials involving approximately 600,000 people between 1966 and 2015. Their findings suggest that individuals at the highest risk, including smokers, those with high cholesterol levels, and older adults with diabetes, would experience the most benefit from treatment, reducing their risk of heart attacks and strokes. Moreover, the report proposes that blood pressure levels could be reduced even further than current targets with treatment. Additionally, the study supports the growing evidence that individuals may benefit from lowering their blood pressure, regardless of their initial levels, through lifestyle changes or medication. However, it indicates that the benefit gained from reducing blood pressure is proportional to the initial level. The authors do not recommend universal medication, but acknowledge the need to consider potential medication side-effects. Prof Liam Smeeth, from the London School of Hygiene and Tropical Medicine, agrees the findings are significant for high-risk individuals. Yet, he emphasizes the importance of considering that not everyone may tolerate low blood pressure levels, and the need to weigh potential drug side-effects against benefits. Heart specialist Dr Tim Chico, of the University of Sheffield, notes that medication is not the only solution. He stresses that we can all reduce our blood pressure by adopting a healthy diet, increasing physical activity, reducing alcohol intake, and maintaining a healthy weight.
A group of six climbers, consisting of three men and three women, were involved in an avalanche on Bidean Nam Bian around 2:00 PM. One male climber raised the alarm. One female climber is in critical condition at Fort William Hospital. It appears the party was descending from a peak on the southern side of the valley, when the slope they were on collapsed. The climbers were near Church Door Buttress when the snow slope gave way, causing five of them to be swept down the mountain and buried under ice and snow. One female climber was found alive but is suffering from severe head injuries. John Grieve, head of the Glencoe mountain rescue team, which coordinated the search, stated that the initial call to authorities was made by two climbers who were not part of the group of six, as they discovered one of the victims in the snow. However, they soon received a call from the male survivor from the climbing party, informing them that more individuals were missing. Mr. Grieve, who was in Spain and did not participate in the search, added: "The first call to police was from two other people who had been on the mountain; they found someone lying next to where they were climbing. It was initially assumed that there was only one casualty, but it became clear that there were others missing when they heard from the survivor." Prayers will be held for the victims during Sunday service at St. Munda's Church, nearby. Reverend Moira Herkes stated that this was one of the worst accidents in the area in many years. "It's very distressing because people come here for enjoyment, and when something like this happens, it affects everyone involved," she said. Scotland's First Minister Alex Salmond described the incident as an "appalling tragedy." "Our immediate thoughts and prayers are with the families of those who have been lost," he said. "Losing four people out of a party of six is heart-wrenching. The Scottish government will offer any assistance we can, and I would like to thank the police and mountain rescue team for their efforts in these challenging circumstances." Relatives concerned about climbers in the area are advised to contact Northern Constabulary's control room at 01463 715555.
Markus Reichel confessed to providing over 200 classified documents to the CIA over a four-year period, receiving at least €80,000 (£63,000, $90,000) in return. These documents included the genuine identities and addresses of German agents stationed abroad. In addition, the Munich court found him guilty of treason for providing three documents to the Russian secret service. Reichel, aged 32, had been employed at the Federal Intelligence Service (BND) since 2007, working in the mail room where he had access to confidential documents. He also had clearance to handle top secret information, as reported by the Munich-based Sueddeutsche Zeitung paper. During his trial, which began in November, Reichel stated that he had handed over the intelligence not just for the excitement and adventure, but also for the recognition. "No-one trusted me with anything at the BND. At the CIA it was different," he told the court. "I would be lying if I said that I didn't like that." His department was responsible for the protection of soldiers deployed abroad, according to Reuters. Between 2008 and 2014, he received between €10,000-€20,000 annually in cash for the secrets he shared at clandestine meeting points in Austria. Reichel admitted to copying sensitive documents at work, smuggling them home where he scanned them and sent them to his handler, as reported by AFP. After several years of this activity, he sought to "experience something new" and offered his services to the Russian consulate in Munich. However, his email to the Russians, containing classified documents, was intercepted, leading to his exposure. In his final statements in court, Reichel apologized and asked for forgiveness, as reported by Sueddeutsche Zeitung. His arrest in 2014 occurred amid strained relations between the US and Germany, following leaks by former CIA agent Edward Snowden revealing the extent of US spying activities in Germany.

At the Football Association's Annual General Meeting held on Wednesday, new regulations have been ratified. These rules will govern players in the top eight tiers of English football, including the Premier League, Championship, Leagues One and Two, Conference, and the top Northern, Southern, and Isthmian leagues. Currently, players are prohibited from wagering on competitions that involve their own club. However, under the forthcoming regulations, players will also be forbidden from disclosing inside information to third parties for betting purposes. Notable players who have previously breached betting regulations include Tottenham's Andros Townsend, Cameron Jerome on loan at Crystal Palace from Stoke last season, and Newcastle's Dan Gosling, who will join Bournemouth next season. In June 2013, Townsend was fined £18,000 by the FA, Jerome received a £50,000 penalty last August, and Gosling was fined £30,000 in March. The new rules, effective from 1 August, extend beyond betting on domestic games. They encompass betting on all global football matches, as well as "football-related matters" such as transfers, managerial appointments, and team selections. Players will no longer be allowed to place bets or disclose inside information about these matters.

The latest "State of Britain's Dormice" report reveals that hazel dormice have become extinct in 17 English counties. Over a period of 25 years, researchers analyzed over 100,000 records collected across the UK. The report indicates that the dormouse is now critically endangered in Britain. Since 1998, trained volunteers have been documenting the presence of this small creature (Muscardinus avellanarius) in various parts of the country. This long-term monitoring project, spanning nearly three decades, is one of the world's longest-running small mammal studies. The dormice primarily inhabit hedgerows and woods, constructing spherical nests in the undergrowth from bark during summer and hibernating on or near the ground in winter, between October and May. Due to their elusive nature, only four dormice are typically found in an area the size of two football fields. A telltale sign of their presence is a nibbled hazelnut. The report underscores the fact that they are harder to find than ever before. Over the past 16 years, their population has declined by nearly 40%. Today, their distribution is limited to the Welsh borders and southern England. They have never been sighted in Scotland or Northern Ireland. Ian White, dormouse officer at the People's Trust for Endangered Species, has been tracking the species for a decade and describes the decline as "dramatic". He states, "Dormice have existed for 40 million years, but their future in Britain is now uncertain, and urgent action is necessary to secure their long-term survival." In 1885, dormice were present in 49 English counties; today, they are known in 32, excluding those counties where they have been reintroduced. White attributes their decline to several key factors, including loss of woodland and hedgerows, habitat fragmentation, changes in farmland and woodland management, and vulnerability to changes in weather, particularly wetter springs and summers, which hinder foraging. Warmer winters also disrupt successful hibernation. White remarks, "This is a disheartening narrative, but there is growing interest in finding solutions and a considerable amount of public enthusiasm to aid in their conservation." BAE Systems announced plans for 17 autonomous flights, utilizing a reconfigured Jetstream 31 airframe. During these flights, human pilots will manage take-off and landing, while the aircraft will operate autonomously during the 300-mile (482km) journey from Lancashire to Inverness. The trials aim to evaluate piloting software and sensor systems, including those designed to monitor clouds and other aircraft. The Jetstream will utilize satellite data and onboard identification systems that detect radio signals from transponders on other planes for self-navigation. Additionally, the aircraft will be equipped with a camera capable of identifying other air users, even if they do not emit warning signals. This camera will also survey the skies to identify potential weather hazards or heavy clouds, allowing the aircraft to alter its course to avoid turbulence and adverse conditions. The aircraft will traverse non-congested airspace at approximately 15,000ft (4.6km) altitude, with the journey anticipated to last around 90 minutes. Maureen McCue, head of BAE's research and technology, expressed excitement about the trials and stated that they were collaborating with the UK's National Air Traffic Services to assess the autonomous aircraft's ability to coexist with human-piloted craft. McCue added that their ultimate goal was to facilitate the operation of unmanned systems in a controlled environment within the UK.

The F-Rating, introduced by Holly Tarquini, director of the Bath Film Festival in 2014, has been adopted by over 40 UK cinemas and festivals. IMDb's Col Needham stated, "The F-Rating serves as an effective means to showcase women both on and off screen." As of now, 21,800 films have been labeled with the F-Rating on IMDb, a film information site that attracts over 250 million visitors monthly. Tarquini explained, "The F-Rating aims to stimulate discussions about the portrayal of women on and off screen." She further added, "It's thrilling when new organizations choose to join us in illuminating the outstanding work women are doing in film and in revealing the film industry's shortcomings in offering equal opportunities to women." The ultimate objective, however, is to reach a point where the F-Rating becomes obsolete because half of the films we see depict stories told by and about women, who have been unfairly underrepresented in the film industry. The Barbican Cinema in London is the latest to adopt the campaign. Curator Gali Gold noted, "The F-Rating offers a straightforward and efficient method to indicate films where stories are told by and about women, and to bring attention to the gender imbalance within the film industry." Anna Navas from Plymouth Arts Centre expressed her enthusiasm, stating, "I incorporated the F-Rating as soon as I learned about it. It's such a clear, engaging, and accessible way to emphasize women on screen that it seemed like a logical choice." The F-Rating was inspired by Alison Bechdel's 1985 comic strip, Dykes to Watch Out For. The cartoon introduced the "Bechdel Test," where characters decided a film should feature at least two women who discuss something other than a man. Films meeting all three criteria, including significant women on screen and written and directed by women, include those with the triple rating. Other films bearing the F-Rating include those directed or written by women.
Many Labour Party members perceive Momentum as an internal faction, a platform for the radical left, and a tool for ousting those opposed to the Corbyn movement. So, who are Momentum and what are their objectives? I attended a gathering of Momentum supporters in Brixton. They do not conform to the stereotypical hard-left image. There was no sign of a Trotskyist beard, and no one attempted to sell me a newspaper. What Steve, Samira, Nadine, and Roland share is an ardor kindled by Jeremy Corbyn's leadership campaign. They are Corbyn's foot soldiers. Steve, a self-proclaimed "middle-aged, BBC Radio 4 devotee," joined the Labour Party immediately following Corbyn's victory. Samira also joined after Corbyn's triumph. "For the first time," she says, "I felt there was someone I could stand behind and trust." Momentum currently boasts approximately 60,000 supporters, operates without a membership fee, primarily through social media, and has around 50 local groups across the UK. Its declared mission is "to create a mass movement for genuine progressive change." However, he believes this move sends a significant message to businesses that Wales remains an attractive destination. Ethan McKen, a 24-year-old resident of Nottingham, suffered an unfortunate accident at a Black Sea resort in Bulgaria on August 8, when he was struck by a wave. As a token of respect, a moment of silence was observed at all matches in the Notts Senior League and the Central Midlands League. McKen was a defender for the Bulwell FC reserve team and taught Physical Education at multiple primary schools in Nottinghamshire's Ashfield district. Ben Moore, manager of Bulwell FC reserves, commented, "The league paid tribute to him, as he had played for various teams within it. He was a resolute and self-assured individual who quickly made an impact on our team." Bulwell FC reserves captain Darrell Hatton added, "He was a gifted player; his sudden demise left us in a state of shock." Friends described McKen as kind and intellectually astute, having earned a first-class honors degree in sports science and management from Nottingham Trent University.

Food Utopia announced plans to halt operations at Avana Bakeries by the end of January. The bakery in Rogerstone has struggled to compete effectively in the market, according to its owners. The Bakers, Food and Allied Workers Union were informed of the proposal on Wednesday. Food Utopia stated that the site has been operating at a loss and is financially unviable. Union representative John James indicated a 45-day consultation process would commence on Thursday. He commented on the oversaturated cake production industry and the health concerns surrounding sugar consumption. In a statement, Food Utopia expressed a commitment to investigating all available options and seeking external support as they discuss the bakery's future. They acknowledged the potential impact on their employees and pledged to provide support during this challenging time. Independent Rogerstone councillor Chris Evans expressed concern over the bakery's longstanding role in the community. He noted that it draws people from various areas, including the valley and Newport, and the implications of the closure would be felt throughout south east Wales. A Welsh Government spokesperson expressed concern over the announcement, particularly given the challenging time of year. They stated their intention to collaborate with the employer and partners to ensure affected employees receive every possible support and assistance. Food Utopia acquired Avana Bakeries in July 2014, after the previous owners warned of potential job losses following the loss of a contract with Marks and Spencer. At the time, there were still 552 employees at the bakery. Reports emerged the following month that Food Utopia planned to cut 390 jobs.

In the early hours of Saturday, around 4:30 GMT, a fire broke out in a rented property in Mill Hill, a town where the incident was reported. The fire spread to two neighboring family homes, causing extensive damage. The rented house was completely destroyed, while the other two properties suffered damage. A family managed to escape from one of the houses, having been alerted by a neighbor. Regrettably, they lost several possessions, including Christmas gifts for their children. Thirty-five firefighters and seven appliances were deployed to extinguish the fire. Preliminary investigations suggest that the fire originated accidentally due to smoking materials. Upon arrival, the first fire crew found a well-established fire in a first-floor bedroom. The occupant had already evacuated, and the firefighters proceeded to evacuate the adjacent houses to prevent any casualties. The fire was contained to the house where it started. Council officials are now cordoning off the properties due to concerns about their structural integrity.
Twitter announced the closure of Vine, the platform that allowed users to share six-second-long video clips on a loop. The company did not provide a reason for the shutdown, but earlier in the day, Twitter revealed it was reducing its workforce by 9% due to slow growth on the social network. In a blog post, Twitter stated, "In the coming months we'll be discontinuing the [Vine] mobile app." Co-founder of Vine, Rus Yusupov, responded on Twitter with, "Don't sell your company!" Twitter acquired Vine before its official launch in 2012 for a reported $30 million. Since then, Twitter has integrated a separate video facility into its primary platform and launched the livestreaming app Periscope. The blog post clarified that the apps, website, and users' Vines would remain accessible and downloadable. Twitter plans to keep the Vine website operational due to the vast amount of incredible content created. Users will be notified before any changes are made to the Vine app or website. Analyst Ian Fogg of tech consultancy IHS Markit commented, "Twitter was all about setting a constraint on communication - 140 characters - and with Vine, it tried to do the same to video. The problem is that Vine didn't keep pace with the innovation from Snapchat, Facebook, and other market players." Dave Lee, North America technology reporter, noted that Vine seemed a natural extension for Twitter when it launched in 2013, but it became clear that Vine could not compete with short videos on Snapchat and Instagram. It is unclear whether Twitter plans to integrate Vine-like features into its main app, but it is unlikely they would abandon the format entirely. Vine has a dedicated fan base and many Vine celebrities, but it is more likely to see a Vine re-shared on Facebook than on Vine itself, which may have contributed to its downfall. Follow Dave Lee on Twitter.
In 2016-17, Cardiff Foodbank distributed 14,568 three-day emergency food supplies, with nearly a third of them going to children. Nationwide in Wales, this figure increased by 11%, with 43% of recipients citing issues with benefits as the primary cause. The Department for Work and Pensions stated that the reasons for food bank usage were "complex" and it was misleading to attribute them to a single issue. Data from the Trussell Trust food bank network, which includes Cardiff, showed a rise in the distribution of emergency food parcels throughout the UK. In Wales, the number rose from 85,656 in 2015-16 to 95,190 in 2016-17. The top three reasons for food bank referrals were delays in benefits, low income, and changes in benefits. Cardiff Foodbank expressed concerns about the rollout of Universal Credit, stating that the six-week or longer wait for a first payment could lead to debt, mental health issues, and rent arrears. The trust has welcomed a "coordinated approach" to Universal Credit rollout in some council areas, such as Torfaen, where the local authority has invited food banks and other charities to form working groups ahead of the new benefit's implementation. Wales was the first nation to complete Universal Credit rollout for single jobseekers and is now beginning with couples and families. Tony Graham, director of devolved nations at the Trussell Trust, expressed interest in the Scottish Government's plans to mitigate the effects of Universal Credit by providing fortnightly payments and making housing payments directly to landlords, and he suggested a conversation with the Welsh Government about how best to support people facing challenges with further Universal Credit rollout in the coming months. Helen Bull, partnership and fundraising manager at Cardiff Foodbank, expressed concern about the continued increase in the number of three-day emergency food supplies provided to local residents in crisis over the past year. She noted that anyone could find themselves in need of the food bank, as people are referred weekly due to unavoidable situations such as illness, delays in benefit payments, or unexpected bills, which make food unaffordable. This year marks the anniversary of England prop Hill's plumbing business, Premier Plumbing Ltd. Known for his destructive play in rugby league, Hill balances his role as captain at Wire with running his business. Hill's interest in plumbing dates back to school, and he approached player welfare manager Karl Fitzpatrick about learning the trade. He started a three-year course around his training and game commitments, running the company with partner Christian Froggat, whom he met during his training. Froggat handles the manual labor, while Hill manages the administrative side, and they both conduct estimates during free evenings. Hill jokingly remarks that Froggat teases him about his tools still having the original packaging. With most of his day free due to training commitments, Hill has afternoons and evenings at his disposal. Warrington coach Tony Smith supports Hill's venture, believing it helps him focus better on rugby. Hill praises the job for allowing him to focus on something else and, in turn, his rugby play. He finds the job rewarding for teaching him life skills in dealing with various people. When Hill moved to Warrington from Leigh for the 2012 season, he couldn't have anticipated a more successful campaign. Warrington won the Challenge Cup for the third time in four years, and Hill was named the club's player of the season, the players' player of the season award, and the Vice President's award in a clean sweep at Warrington's awards night. Although the team has not won a trophy since, Hill is determined to make this visit to Wembley a triumphant one. Hill has avoided discussing Wembley this week, focusing instead on his family's travel arrangements. His eldest son, aged seven, will walk out with him, and everyone in the house is excited for the trip.
Brianna Rollins, aged 25, was absent from a test to participate in 'Brianna Rollins Day' in September, her hometown in Florida. A gold medalist in the 100m hurdles at the Rio Olympics, Rollins is suspended until December 18th. As a result, she will be unable to compete in the World Championships in London in August. In a statement on Instagram, Rollins expressed that this is one of the most challenging periods in her career, particularly after achieving a successful 2016 season. The United States Anti-Doping Agency (USADA) claims that Rollins failed to submit her required whereabouts information for drug testers. According to World Anti-Doping Agency regulations, an athlete cannot miss more than three tests within a 12-month period. Rollins missed one test in April 2016 due to travel, and two in September – one during a visit to the White House and the other upon her return to Florida. USADA has ruled that her results from September 27th – the date of her third whereabouts failure – will be disqualified. However, the world champion will be permitted to retain the Olympic medal she earned in August. "This is a challenging case due to the imposition of a severe penalty on a talented athlete who is not accused or suspected of using any prohibited substances," USADA stated in their ruling.

Scrapped parking charges at Glan Clwyd Hospital in Bodelwyddan have ended with the conclusion of an external contract. This move follows a promise by the Welsh Assembly Government that parking would be free at nearly every NHS hospital in Wales by the end of 2011. Hospitals with private parking management had to cut costs until contracts expired. At Glan Clwyd, these changes coincide with a new parking system designed to make parking more convenient for patients and visitors. Parking will remain at the hospital's front, near the main public entrances, with additional parking available in the car park on the right side of the access road. Designated parking areas for the renal, cancer, and maternity units will persist, free of time limits or charges. The adjustments for accessible parking for the disabled will not be impacted by these changes. New signs are being installed to guide the public to the designated parking areas. The rest of the parking spaces on the site will be allocated for staff. A hospital spokesperson stated, "We understand that the new system will require time to fully develop and become routine. In the interim, our primary focus is to minimize disruption to patients and visitors as the new arrangements are implemented."
Monitor initiated an investigation into the management of The Christie NHS Foundation Trust on the 8th of March, citing concerns over the trust's governance. Stephen Hay, from Monitor, stated that the trust was experiencing significant issues, and their investigation had uncovered concerns regarding the board's operations. However, Hay emphasized that there were no concerns about the quality of care provided by The Christie. The trust has declined to comment. Hay, the managing director of provider regulation at Monitor, further explained that while there were no concerns about the care, it was crucial for patients, taxpayers, and staff that the trust be effectively managed. The investigation into the trust followed the resignation of its chairman, Lord Bradley, in February. The trust's CEO, Caroline Shaw, has been under suspension since November due to an internal disciplinary investigation, but Monitor clarified that its inquiries did not involve any allegations relating to Ms. Shaw. Monitor has appointed Sir Hugh Taylor, chair of Guy's and St Thomas' NHS Foundation Trust, as interim chairman of The Christie. Under the Health and Social Care Act 2012, Monitor has the authority to require foundation trusts to make senior appointments if it deems it to be in the best interests of patients. Previously, Monitor had expressed concerns about whether the trust had violated its license to provide healthcare services by failing to uphold the principles of good governance. There were concerns that the board of the trust had not followed the necessary corporate governance standards. Although The Christie declined to comment on Monitor's findings, it welcomed its new chairman. In a statement, the hospital expressed hope that Sir Hugh's appointment, along with his experience and expertise, would bring a swift and satisfactory resolution to the ongoing situation. The trust assured that its operations continued to be delivered to the highest standards, and patients, families, and carers could be reassured that the situation would not affect or compromise patient care. Manchester Withington MP John Leech previously described the situation as a "mess." Leech emphasized his primary concern was ensuring that patients came first. The Yonhap news agency, which has close ties to South Korea's government and is publicly funded, reported that a military source claimed every part of Pyongyang would be annihilated by ballistic missiles and high-explosive shells. This assertion comes after North Korea conducted its fifth and largest nuclear test on Friday. The international community is currently deliberating on a response. The US is considering imposing additional sanctions, beyond those imposed by the UN Security Council, Japan, and South Korea. In response, North Korea dismissed these threats as "meaningless sanctions... highly laughable." A South Korean military official told Yonhap that districts believed to be harboring North Korea's leadership would be primary targets in any attack. The official stated that the city would be reduced to ashes and erased from the map. This rhetoric mirrors the bloodcurdling language that North Korea frequently uses about the South Korean government in Seoul. There has been increasing criticism within South Korea of the government as its efforts to isolate the North have failed to curb leader Kim Jong-un's nuclear ambitions. Following Friday's nuclear test, news of South Korea's attack plan for the North is believed to have been shared with parliament. Meanwhile, the US's special envoy for North Korea, Sung Kim, stated that Washington is considering taking unilateral action against Pyongyang. Kim asserted, "North Korea continues to present a growing threat to the region, to our allies, to ourselves, and we will do everything possible to defend against that growing threat." He also mentioned that the US, Japan, and South Korea would be exploring unilateral measures, bilateral measures, and potential trilateral cooperation. North Korea is prohibited by the UN from any tests of nuclear or missile technology and has faced five sets of UN sanctions since its first test in 2006. North Korea claimed that Friday's test was of a "nuclear warhead that has been standardized to be able to be mounted on strategic ballistic rockets." Estimates of the explosive yield of the latest blast have varied. South Korea's military estimates it to be around 10 kilotonnes, making it North Korea's strongest nuclear test to date. A win for the Wallabies against the hosts on October 10th would secure Wales' spot in the quarterfinals. Warren Gatland's team is determined to emerge victorious in this match, as stated by kicking coach Jenkins. "Our focus is squarely on the match against Australia a week from Saturday, regardless of the outcome tomorrow," he said. "I'm not expressing a preference for the Australians. Whatever transpires – whether England or Australia wins tomorrow – we must view it as a challenge. We need to show up a week from Saturday and win; it's as straightforward as that." Wales, England, and Australia all have a chance to advance to the quarter-finals, but only the top two in the pool will proceed. A win grants four points, a team scoring four or more tries in a match earns a bonus point, and a loss by seven points or fewer yields one point. The possibilities are numerous. If England defeats Australia, the hosts would be favored for their final game against Uruguay on the same day, while both Wales and the Wallabies recorded bonus-point victories over Uruguay. A bonus-point win for England would make the match between Australia and Wales earlier in the day at Twickenham decisive for the other qualifier from the "pool of death." There is a potential scenario where Wales and England could end up with the same points. If this were to occur, Wales would advance due to their victory in the previous pool match. Should Australia lose to England and then defeat Wales, there is also a possibility of all three teams ending up with the same points, at which point the points difference would be considered. Jenkins, who was the first player to score 1,000 points in international rugby, and whose Wales tally of 1,049 remains a national record, mentioned that none of the Wales management team would watch the England vs Australia game, with Jenkins himself planning to watch it at home. "Regardless of what happens tomorrow – if England were to lose and be eliminated – we'd still be looking forward to the following week's game because it's a crucial match for us," he said. Tidal Lagoon Power disclosed to BBC Wales that on the same day an independent review was initiated, they received a letter from a minister. Mark Shorrock, the CEO, stated that the cost of the project could now be distributed over a period of 90 years instead of 35 years. The UK government declined to comment on the letter. The Swansea lagoon, set to be the first of six around the British coastline, is said to potentially generate 8% of the UK's electricity with a lifespan of 120 years. The company also aims to develop lagoons at five other locations across the UK, including three in Wales. Mr. Shorrock told BBC Wales that they have a strong case and believe the review will demonstrate the viability of tidal energy in the UK. On the day of the announcement last week, he received a letter from Energy Secretary Amber Rudd, which he asserted indicated the UK government's readiness to consider long-term funding for the project and future lagoons. He stated that he had provided extensive information to the UK government, which will now be evaluated independently, while negotiations on the electricity strike price are being finalized. "We welcome the review because it will establish and confirm that affordable power can be derived from our indigenous energy sources - our tides in the Severn and Liverpool Bay," he said. The review is set to release its findings in the autumn. The construction work has already been delayed by a year due to stalled negotiations over the amount of public funding required. The company had been advocating for a decision on a guaranteed price for the energy they would produce to be made by next month. However, the review, commencing this spring, will not provide any answers before at least the end of 2016. Energy Minister Lord Bourne has stated that the review will bring clarity. "I aim to ascertain whether tidal lagoons can be cost-effective and what their impact on bills will be - both in the short term and the long term," he said. Source: Tidal Lagoon Power Ltd.

For another nine days to pass, the residents of Eglwyswrw, a village close to Cardigan, would surpass a Scottish record set in 1923 for the longest consecutive period of rainfall, which stood at 89 days. John Davies, a farmer and local Pembrokeshire councilor in Eglwyswrw, expressed his hope that this record would not be broken, as the persistent rain had become "exhausting." The forecast for Saturday suggested that it could remain dry, potentially bringing an end to the rainy spell. "We are still in the running, but hopefully, this will be our last day," said Mr. Davies on Friday. "This is a record we don't wish to hold. The prolonged rain takes a toll on both man and beast, and 81 days of it is challenging." The increased sales of raincoats and boots at shopkeeper Brian Llewelyn's store are a testament to the prolonged wet weather. "An ill wind doesn't always bring good, but at least it's been beneficial for sales of rain gear," he said. He added that the continuous rain was "disheartening" and had negatively impacted other local businesses, such as builders and farmers, who have had to bring livestock indoors. Although the Met Office does not keep official records for consecutive days of rain, its weather stations do record rain data. The nearby automated Whitechurch station, covering Eglwyswrw, shows rain every day since October 26, although some readings are as low as 0.2mm. The previous longest rain-stricken period was 89 days in a row on the Scottish island of Islay in 1923. A Met Office spokesperson attributed the high rainfall in Eglwyswrw to its location near the Preseli Hills and the mild, wet weather that has set records this winter, resulting in the village receiving more than its fair share of rain. In Wales, December's rainfall for a single month was only surpassed once before - in November 1929. Mr. Davies concluded, "We are a resilient community here in Eglwyswrw, and it takes more than a few showers to wear us down, but it has been, in all seriousness, quite wearing."
Adam Peaty, aged 22, broke new ground by swimming under 26 seconds for the first time, completing the race in 25.95 seconds while defending his World Championship title in Hungary. Speaking to BBC East Midlands Today, Peaty indicated that he could potentially shave 0.3 seconds off his start time. If he can execute all his strategies perfectly, he is entering incredibly swift territory. The swimmer based in Loughborough had previously retained his 100m title and also won a silver medal in the 100m mixed medley, bringing his World Championship medal count to six – five gold and one silver. "There's always room for improvement," Peaty remarked. "Whether that happens in a year, three years, or five, I am quite certain it will eventually." Peaty expressed surprise at his new 50m world record set in the semi-final, achieved just a few hours after he had broken the record in the morning heats. He still has "Project 56" on his agenda, a personal goal to become the first man to break the 57-second barrier in the 100m. Peaty emphasized that he has no plans to set boundaries on how fast he can go in either event. "To achieve 25.9 is astonishing," he added. "I was fairly confident, but not that confident. The only other person close to that is 26.5, and a difference of 0.6 seconds over a 50 is a massive amount of time." Before focusing on his future achievements, Peaty acknowledged the importance of taking a break. "The training regimen is demanding day in and day out," he said. "It's crucial for me to relax now, go on holiday, enjoy myself, and celebrate. It is vital to return next year with a clear mind."

A recently published report from a health organization reveals that increasing prices by 20% or more leads to reduced consumption and allegedly enhanced nutrition. This body, which advocates for global health, has earlier suggested limiting sugar consumption, but has refrained from endorsing taxation measures. Countries such as Mexico and Hungary have already implemented taxes on sugar-added products, and South Africa plans to introduce a sugar tax next year, making it the sole African nation to do so. The World Health Organization (WHO) has expressed its desire to see a decrease in the consumption of "free sugars," stating that this reduction would lower the occurrence of obesity, diabetes, and tooth decay. "Free sugars" encompass all types of sugar in one's diet, except for those naturally found in fruit and milk. Dr. Francesco Branca, the WHO's nutrition director, stated that nutritionally, people do not require any sugar in their diet. He proposed that sugar intake should not exceed 10% of a person's total calorie intake, and ideally, it should be below 5%. However, the organization suggested that financial measures like taxes should be applied only to items that have healthier alternatives available. The report's conclusions are based on a gathering of global experts and a review of existing evidence. Additionally, the report found that government subsidies for fruits and vegetables, which lower prices, can boost the amount consumed. Furthermore, the same tax measures applied to sugary drinks seem to be effective for other sugary foods, as well as those high in saturated fats, trans fats, and salt.
A lavishly adorned gourd, long believed to house a handkerchief soaked in the late King Louis XVI's blood following his execution by guillotine in 1793, is now thought to be a fraudulent artifact. Scientists have sequenced the genome of the sample and have expressed doubt about its royal origin. The study is published in Scientific Reports. The researchers suspect that the gourd and its contents were likely created by an 18th-century con artist aiming to profit from a revolutionary memento. Prof. Carles Lalueza-Fox, from the Institute of Evolutionary Biology in Barcelona, Spain, stated, "During the French Revolution, the guillotine was in constant operation, and it was easier to approach the scaffold during the executions of lesser individuals. It's possible that this was one such occasion, where someone attempted to pass off a souvenir as a genuine relic from the revolutionary era." The blood-stained cloth was stored within a gourd adorned with images of revolutionary heroes and inscribed with the text, "On January 21, Maximilien Bourdaloue dipped his handkerchief in the blood of Louis XVI after his decapitation." Initial forensic tests suggested the possibility of this being the blood of the French king. However, this latest research raises questions about its authenticity. To examine the sample, scientists scrutinized sections of the genome related to physical characteristics. Portraits of Louis XVI depict him with blue eyes, but this sample appears to belong to someone more likely to have had brown eyes. Prof. Lalueza-Fox noted, "The probability of this person having blue eyes is very low - it is approximately 3%." Historical records, including correspondence from Louis XVI's wife, Marie-Antoinette, also state that the king was exceptionally tall. While the average height was around 167cm (5ft 5in) at that time, the King was believed to be at least 185cm (6ft 1in) tall. Prof. Lalueza-Fox added, "While we don't fully understand the genetic basis of height, we do know the genetic markers in extreme cases for very tall or very short individuals. However, this sample lacks the excess of markers that could be

William Thomas Cosgrave, Ireland's first president of the Executive Council, or the country's first prime minister, served from 1922 to 1932. He guided the newly established state through its initial turbulent years post-Irish War of Independence with Britain. Regrettably, his headstone at Goldenbridge Cemetery in Inchicore has been vandalized, causing significant damage not only to his own monument but also to 12 other headstones dating back to Victorian and pre-Victorian eras. This is not the first time Cosgrave's burial site has been desecrated, as his grave was also damaged in 2014. Cosgrave ascended to power during the Irish Civil War, a fierce internal conflict between supporters of the 1921 Anglo-Irish Treaty and the establishment of a Free State, and those advocating for a completely independent republic free from British influence. Although he participated in the 1916 Easter Rising rebellion, he later supported the treaty and defended the new Free State vehemently. During the Civil War, 77 republican prisoners were executed under his leadership, a number far exceeding the 16 rebels formally executed by the British post-1916 rebellion. Cosgrave's legacy remains controversial, with some viewing him as ruthless while others see him as a strong leader and a key architect of Irish independence. He passed away in 1965 and was given a state funeral before being buried at Goldenbridge Cemetery. His son, Liam Cosgrave, who later served as prime minister from 1973 to 1977, visited the grave to assess the damage following the recent incident. The Cosgrave family expressed regret over the incident. The cemetery is managed by the Glasnevin Trust. John Green, the chairman of the charity, stated that the 2014 attack coincided with the publication of a biography on Cosgrave, but the motive for the latest incident remains unclear. He added that there is no evidence suggesting the damage to the Cosgrave plot was politically motivated, despite the upcoming centenary of the Easter Rising. Another grave, belonging to a child who perished during the Easter Rising, was also targeted in the attack

Emotional after the game, he shared, "I couldn't have scripted it any better... I managed just to get outside Barnes and cross the line. It's an incredible feeling scoring a try, but knowing it's your last chance to score, it is just fantastic." He expressed, "Gail brought the kids on, and it was fantastic to spend the lap of honor with them." He also admitted to being more nervous for this, his 87th and final Wales appearance, than at any other point in his career. Extending his Wales try-scoring record to 58 in 87 games with that injury-time try, Williams said, "For me personally, I've just been more excited than I've ever been for a game, certainly more nervous." He found it difficult to sleep the night before and was up at 5:30-6:00 AM, a rarity for him. Despite the emotional turmoil, Williams emphasized that he didn't want the game to be about him. He wanted it to be about Wales winning. He praised his team's effort, particularly when they were playing against one of the best teams in the world and were down to 14 men due to a sin-bin. Even in a defeat, Williams was proud of his team-mates' spirit. He concluded, "The crowd's been fantastic and it has been from the first moment I played for Wales and [it was] certainly no different today - probably I've never sensed or felt anything like that in my life. The mayor lacks the power to enact a pedicab ban, thus he is pursuing governmental legislation to address this issue. Additionally, he aims to decrease the number of minicabs, a proposal that the Licensed Taxi Drivers Association supports. In 2014, it's estimated that approximately 13,000 new private hire drivers were added to London's fleet, partly due to the increasing popularity of budget-friendly car booking apps like Uber. Since December 2012, Mayor Johnson has advocated for a pedicab ban, citing concerns that they congest city streets and regularly compromise passenger safety. On any given night in the West End, one can easily spot the distinctive bells of rickshaws (officially known as pedicabs) soliciting customers. Although some tourists and the occasional inebriated businessman seem to appreciate them, authorities have long sought their removal. While there are reputable operators, there's also a reckless sector where safety concerns and overcharging complaints are prevalent. In 2002, the black cabbies unsuccessfully attempted to have pedicabs banned in court. Pedicabs operate under a loophole in the Metropolitan Public Carriage Act of 1869, classified as stage carriages rather than Hackney cabs, which allows them to solicit passengers. If the mayor wishes to ban pedicabs, he must revise the relevant legislation. This process will likely take time and may involve legal challenges.
Lindsay Newell, a resident of Burton-upon-Trent, neglected several animals that subsequently became emaciated, for which she received a two-year conditional discharge at Stafford Magistrates' Court. She was also prohibited from keeping certain animals, including sheep, goats, pigs, and equine animals, and ordered to pay £2,000 in costs. The judge stated that the neglect was not intentional and cleared her of 25 charges of failing to feed animals. The court found that Newell, who worked at Burton Wildlife Rescue and Animal Centre in Etwall, Derbyshire, failed to monitor the weight loss of six animals. One of these animals was a pig named Babe, who was rescued from a Derby council house and made national news. Babe died in front of RSPCA officers and the police during a raid in November 2012. District Judge David Taylor explained that Newell put herself under pressure and financial strain due to her desire to help animals. He further stated that her actions were not deliberate or intentional, but rather a result of her trying to care for too many animals of various species. Newell reportedly spent £300 a week on food and straw from her earnings as a veterinary nurse, but has since lost her job. Defence lawyer Nigel Weller stated that Newell now wishes to dedicate her life to running the sanctuary. The rescue center remains open, housing hundreds of animals, such as cats, pigeons, chickens, rabbits, and crows. The RSPCA spent £20,000 on investigating the case and bringing Newell to court, and she is required to pay £2,000 in costs.

During the trial at Glasgow's High Court, Dr. William Stewart testified about Kimberley MacKenzie's autopsy. He stated that there was evidence of bruising, bleeding, and swelling on the right side of her brain, as well as a piece of bone that appeared to have been forcefully embedded. The couple on trial, Steven Jackson and Michelle Higgins, are accused of murdering and dismembering Ms. MacKenzie in Montrose on October 27, 2015. Dr. Stewart examined the brain on December 10, 2015. He told the jury that, beyond the visible injuries, there had been an impact-induced bone fragment. The prosecutor, Ashley Edwards QC, questioned Dr. Stewart about the time between Ms. MacKenzie's injury and her death. Dr. Stewart responded that while textbooks suggest this period could be three to four hours, his conservative estimate was an hour or less. He also stated that, given proper medical care, the head injury could potentially be survivable. Defense QC Donald Findlay, representing Mr. Jackson, proposed that changes in the brain due to decay could account for Dr. Stewart's findings, suggesting that Ms. MacKenzie may have died shortly after being injured. Dr. Stewart countered by stating that the brain did not conceal the usual signs of decay. The defendants are charged with murdering Ms. MacKenzie by repeatedly striking her with a hammer or similar object and stabbing her multiple times. They are also accused of dismembering her body and concealing parts of it in various locations in Montrose between October 27 and November 4, 2015. The trial, presided over by Judge Lady Rae, is ongoing.

This year, insurance company Admiral sponsored the tree, but it will not be in place for this year's event on Thursday night. Instead, the tree will not be set up until November 25th, as it is being shipped from China. David Hughes-Lewis, an independent retailer in Cardiff, expressed his disappointment, stating, "It seems a bit odd - turning on all the Christmas lights and there's no tree." Cardiff councillor Jayne Cowan echoed these sentiments, saying, "Our residents and visitors want to immerse themselves in the Christmas spirit, and the absence of a tree will not contribute to this." A council spokesman confirmed that they have secured a 40m (131ft) tree, which will serve as the "centerpiece of our festive decorations" outside Cardiff Castle. The Step into Christmas event will still take place, featuring a street parade, the opening of Winter Wonderland, and market stalls.
Twelve-year-old Chris Whitehead, a pupil at Impington Village College close to Cambridge, expressed his discontent with the school's dress code that prohibits boys from wearing shorts during hot weather. Chris, a student in year 8, claimed he discovered a rule exemption and attended school in a skirt as a demonstration. In response, the school has promised to reevaluate the policy later in the year. Chris commented, "There's been some jesting, but I don't mind if people mock me if I'm standing up for something I believe in. I think people support me, and I hope things will change." He further explained, "I reviewed the uniform policy, and it doesn't specify that only girls should wear skirts, so I utilized this to my advantage. It was a peaceful protest." Some of Chris' schoolmates considered his action unusual yet courageous. A school representative commended his "independence" and "individuality." Chris' father, Brian Whitehead, expressed pride, stating they inquired about his decision but found Chris to be resolute. Chris shared with the BBC his aspirations for a future career in politics, beginning with the House of Commons. Since garnering media attention, Chris has received significant interest on Twitter. Television presenter Phillip Schofield tweeted, "Kudos to 12-year-old Chris Whitehead for protesting the school rule that permits girls to wear skirts in summer but denies boys the same privilege by wearing a skirt himself. Brave move and a valid point. He aspires to be a politician! I believe we will profit from his intelligence."
George Black, who is reportedly earning nearly £170,000 annually, is anticipated to depart by the end of 2014. At the age of 61, Mr. Black has overseen some preparations for the Commonwealth Games and dealt with the effects of limited council funding. The selection process for his successor will commence. Mr. Black has been employed with Glasgow City Council, as well as its previous structure, for over 20 years. Prior to his tenure in Glasgow, the qualified accountant worked for the Hydro Electric Board and various other councils. In a message to staff, Mr. Black stated: "I have served at a senior level in Glasgow for over 20 years and have personally observed the city's progress. However, much is still left to be accomplished, and I believe that now is the ideal time for a new chief executive to address the challenges and opportunities that are on the horizon. It has been a great honor to have been the chief executive during such an exciting period, and I have been fortunate to have the support of numerous dedicated colleagues." Glasgow City Council leader Gordon Matheson commented: "I would like to express my gratitude to George for his exceptional service on behalf of the city."

As a result, he was unable to participate in the US Open. In the upcoming tournament, he is scheduled to face France's Richard Gasquet in the opening round. The 28-year-old Nadal expressed his optimism, stating, "I feel much better, I am in good shape. I am trying to forget about my wrist." He further added that whenever he returns from an injury, he is motivated with an extra sense of determination. His last competitive match was a fourth-round defeat against Australian Nick Kyrgios at Wimbledon. Although his wrist is not yet fully healed, Nadal asserted that the injury does not hinder his ability to compete. He explained, "I only feel the wrist a little when I start, when I begin to play every day, but then it disappears." The world's top-ranked player, Novak Djokovic, is the top seed in the upcoming tournament in Beijing. British player Andy Murray is also set to compete in the event, which commences on Monday.
Daley secured his first individual World Championship bronze medal since 2009, following his team gold win with Rebecca Gallantree in the team event. He expressed his satisfaction, stating, "I'm really pleased with this bronze as I made things challenging for myself." After being ninth after the second round, Daley managed a strong comeback. The 21-year-old, who had already earned a spot for Team GB in the Olympic 10m platform by reaching the final, executed four outstanding routines, scoring a total of 537.95 and securing a spot on the final podium. This result boosted Britain's total to four medals, their best performance at a world championships. Previously, they had won one medal in 2005 and 2009. Defending champion Qui Bo of China (587.0) clinched the title, with USA Olympic gold medallist David Boudia (560.2) finishing second. Daley, who won bronze at London 2012, added, "I've learned to persist, stay focused, and keep going because you never know what can happen in competitions." He further mentioned, "It came down to the last dive when we were level, but I enjoy that competition pressure - I find it exciting." Daley also commented on the podium's consistency, stating, "It's interesting to see the same three people on the podium today as at London 2012. It seems we've still got it, and we just need to rearrange ourselves for next year, hoping I can end up in the top position!"
Mark Frost, a 70-year-old retired English teacher, confessed to sexually abusing nine children in Thailand between 2009 and 2012. He admitted to 23 charges at the Old Bailey, having pleaded guilty to 22 charges last year. Six of the charges pertain to the abuse of two students at a school in Worcestershire during the 1980s and 1990s. Frost will be sentenced on Thursday. His legal proceedings were initiated following an international investigation conducted by the UK's National Crime Agency (NCA), in collaboration with authorities in Thailand, Spain, and the Netherlands. Frost sexually assaulted impoverished Asian boys, offering them money, sweets, computer games, and swims in his pool to groom them, before coercing them into sexual acts. He fled prosecution in Thailand but was extradited from Spain last year after Dutch police discovered evidence of his activities on a man's computer in the Netherlands. The boys, aged between 10 and 14, were coerced into giving thumbs-up signs and heart gestures while being filmed on a webcam engaging in sexual acts. The court also heard details of Frost's abuse of two students at a school in Worcestershire during the late 1980s and 1990s. He had sexual encounters with the boys in a school storeroom, during breaks, at his home, at a car park in Woking, Surrey, and elsewhere. One of the victims has since passed away, while the other stated that he lived in constant fear following the abuse. Frost admitted to charges that included multiple rapes, sex assaults, inciting children to engage in sexual activity, and making indecent pictures. Prosecutor Sally-Ann Hales revealed that images and web chats seized from Frost's Dutch contact featured 15 boys, nine of whom were identified and interviewed. The boys' mothers expressed their "sorrow" at learning that the man they considered a "kind and generous foreigner" had abused their children. One of the boys was too ashamed to tell his mother and had become "withdrawn and sometimes aggressive." Wales is scheduled to play two matches in the Pacific Islands, one against Tonga and the other against Samoa in June. However, there are still some issues to address with Tonga, as there is currently no pitch available. The necessary stadium infrastructure is not yet in place, and World Rugby and the Welsh Rugby Union (WRU) are meeting again to discuss the matter. The game against Samoa is set for Apia on June 24 with fewer concerns. In Tonga, WRU representatives inspected the facilities in December, but the pitch was still incomplete, and concerns about medical cover persist. World Rugby has stated that a new venue is due to be constructed there, but it remains to be seen if it will be ready in time for the fixture. An alternative venue could be Auckland, New Zealand, as the facilities around the Tongan stadium are not yet up to standard. The return of the Wales A team is facing a delay due to a lack of opposition. Initially, it was announced that the second-string national side would return by January 2015, but the WRU has been unable to find suitable opponents. The window for playing is currently the last week of January. If no other fixture can be arranged, Wales may play England or Ireland in early 2018. Both nations have expressed their willingness to play, and the WRU is now focusing on contracting one of them. If another fixture can be found, the WRU is in discussions with other parties about it. Mike Ruddock was the last head coach of the Wales A team, leading them to a 30-23 win over Scotland in 2002.
Law enforcement officials in Bethesda have attempted to address groups of individuals who have been leaving broken bottles and litter, but the situation has escalated recently. PCSO Gareth Davies of North Wales Police expressed concern over the community's "awful" deterioration due to such behavior. However, some locals argued that local youths had few alternatives for recreation. In response, North Wales Police has implemented a dispersal order, granting officers the authority to instruct anyone to vacate the area if their conduct is disruptive. Mr. Davies explained to BBC Radio Wales' Good Morning Wales that the aim is to prevent an individual from Bethesda from facing prosecution or future consequences from a dispersal order, as they are in an age where they believe they are too old for youth clubs but too young for pubs. One unidentified resident expressed worry about her young son getting hurt due to the numerous shards of glass in the parks. Yet, another resident voiced concerns that the enforcement would not be effective, as it could potentially criminalize the town's youth. She suggested that the youngsters, who she described as being "a little hyperactive and having nothing to do," need a secure place to go.
The revised logo consists of two horizontal white bars and an exclamation mark against a pink backdrop. It has been met with criticism on Twitter due to its perceived resemblance to the Roman numeral representation of "BBC 2!". BBC Three's marketing head, Nikki Carr, acknowledged the criticism but expressed no concern, stating, "Some individuals are resistant to change, and we aimed to be audacious and create something modern and long-lasting." She further noted that the logo must be compatible with both television broadcast and app icons, citing Snapchat as an example of a successful brand without incorporating its name in its logo. Ms. Carr admitted that the BBC, as depicted in the satirical show W1A, faces a curse when it comes to marketing. Some have observed a similarity between the new logo and a sketch from W1A where the team proposed replacing the BBC logo with three bars. However, Ms. Carr clarified that the three bars were chosen to symbolize the three principles upon which the new channel is built: "Think... Laugh... Speak," with the exclamation mark representing the latter's emphasis on giving a voice to young people. Ms. Carr announced that young people will be involved in the decision-making process at the channel and will contribute as content creators. In the upcoming weeks, the BBC will collaborate with 50 young creative individuals. The content to be produced will encompass short films, blogs, animation, picture-led stories, and will be delivered daily via soon-to-be-launched products. In November, the BBC Trust approved plans to move BBC Three online as part of the corporation's cost-cutting measures. It was agreed that long-form programs would be aired on BBC One and Two, accounting for approximately two hours weekly. As of February 16, BBC Three will transition into a promotional channel, informing viewers about online content, with the BBC Three TV channel expected to go dark in the following weeks.
Researchers presenting their findings on the supposed discovery in the Polish town of Walbrzych suggested the possibility of a tunnel, but no train. One individual who claimed to have found the train maintains his belief that it remains hidden. It was alleged that the train was concealed underground near Wroclaw as Soviet forces approached in 1945. The Nazis had constructed numerous tunnels in the Walbrzych area during World War II. In August, Deputy Culture Minister Piotr Zuchowski expressed a 99% conviction that a German military train was buried near Walbrzych, based on ground-penetrating radar images which appeared to show a train armed with gun turrets. However, Professor Janusz Madej from Krakow's Academy of Mining, following a geological survey of the site, stated that no evidence of a train was found. "There may be a tunnel. There is no train," he declared at a press conference in Walbrzych. Local legends speak of an armored train transporting gold from what is now the Polish city of Wroclaw, which supposedly vanished near Ksiaz castle, 3km (two miles) from Walbrzych. Earlier this year, Piotr Koper from Poland and Andreas Richter from Germany informed authorities of their knowledge of the train's location. They stipulated through their lawyers that they desired 10% of the value of any discovered items. At Tuesday's news conference, Mr. Koper expressed doubts about the survey methodology and reiterated his belief that the train was still there.

I believe that in these situations, the whole-life sentence is a suitable choice for the judiciary, and they should be guided to impose such sentences. Our petition, 'Life Means Life,' calls for judges to have the option for whole-life sentencing in specific circumstances." In February 2013, the education department of Torfaen Council came under supervision by the education watchdog Estyn. This was due to insufficient progress following an inspection in 2011, during which significant shortcomings were identified and an unsatisfactory rating was given. After subsequent evaluations and necessary corrective actions, the supervision was lifted on Friday. In 2013, Torfaen became the sixth Welsh council to be placed under special measures, following Anglesey, Blaenau Gwent, Pembrokeshire, Monmouthshire, and Merthyr Tydfil. Currently, only Merthyr Tydfil remains in special measures. Education Minister Huw Lewis commented, "I am encouraged by the good progress we are witnessing with local authorities being removed from special measures, and I hope this will serve as a catalyst for future success." In a letter to Torfaen's chief executive, Alison Ward, Clive Phillips, an assistant director at Estyn, mentioned that inspectors reviewed seven recommendations from inspections in 2011 and 2013. These recommendations urged the council to enhance standards in secondary schools and provide more opportunities for school leavers who do not secure jobs or training. The authority also faced criticism for standards at the GCSE level. A report stated that over half of schools were in the bottom quarter for performance in the core subjects of English or Welsh, maths, and science. No school exceeded the average in terms of the proportion of pupils achieving the equivalent of five GCSEs at grades A* to C. After being placed under special measures, the Welsh government mandated the creation of a recovery board to assist and monitor the council as it addressed the issues. In his letter, Mr. Phillips stated that the council, elected members, and the recovery board had worked collaboratively to improve these areas. He added, "As a result, Her Majesty's Chief Inspector of Education and Training in Wales believes that the authority no longer requires special measures and is removing it from further follow-up activity." Torfaen council's executive member for education, David Yeowell, expressed delight at this news, which he believed reflected well on the combined efforts of school colleagues and the education service.
Forensic scientist Samantha Ho, aged 39, was discovered deceased at her residence in Curlew Place, St Neots, on the 29th of August. Her head and upper body were found separately, and a subsequent autopsy revealed that she perished due to injuries to her neck. Her spouse, Timothy Allen, 40, of Curlew Place, pleaded guilty to manslaughter by diminished responsibility in a hearing at the Old Bailey earlier. He had initially denied her murder at a previous hearing in December. He will be sentenced on the 17th of March. The authorities were initially alerted to the house by the emergency services following a report of distress at the property. Armed response teams gained entry to the house, where Ms. Ho's body was discovered. Mr. Allen was apprehended on suspicion of murder and was transported to a hospital with an injury described as serious but not life-threatening. He was subsequently charged with the murder of his wife. Detective Chief Inspector Richard Wall of Cambridgeshire Police stated, "This is a heartbreaking case where a life was lost, and families have been left devastated." In a statement, Ms. Ho's family described her as "widely admired... with a promising future filled with aspirations." The alumna of Nottingham Trent University had been employed at bio-science firm Asterand, in Royston, Hertfordshire, for over a decade. Prior to that, she was employed at Pharmagene, which is part of Asterand, and Cambridge firm Cytocell. "Samantha aspired to be a distinguished scientist, travel extensively, fulfill her dreams, and spend more time with her family," Ms. Ho's family said. "Unfortunately, on that fateful day... Samantha was tragically taken from us. That day marked the loss of a part of us."
NFU Scotland conducted inspections at Tesco, Asda, Sainsbury's, Morrisons, and Marks & Spencer stores. Nigel Miller, the union's president, emphasized the need for sheep farmers to receive reassurance that their product is appreciated. He suggested that a retailer's pledge to support Scottish lamb could contribute to the industry's revival. The union acknowledged the difficulties faced by sheep farmers, as sales dwindle in autumn and prices do not increase before Christmas. Over the past six months, it has been monitoring supermarkets' commitments to domestic lamb. Morrisons was commended for consistently stocking only Scottish or British lamb. The union also recognized marketing efforts by Marks & Spencer and Sainsbury's. However, it criticized Tesco and Asda for stocking some Scottish or British produce, yet still carrying substantial quantities of New Zealand and Australian lamb. Miller stated, "This is a crucial time for sheep farmers to receive encouragement from their major clients, the UK supermarkets, with a clear indication that their product is sought after and valued. Morrisons demonstrates what can be achieved with a complete dedication to Scottish or British produce in the stores we visited, as packs of lamb are sold at prices comparable to competitors on the shop shelves. This starkly contrasts with the persistent presence of New Zealand and Australian lamb on the shelves of Tesco and Asda, even during our peak marketing season in Scotland, when our lamb is at its freshest and most flavorful." He further emphasized the potential for supermarkets to boost their stocks of Scots lamb, "With lambing only a few months away, such an action would send a positive message to producers and help alleviate some of the gloom generated by one of the more challenging seasons on record." A Tesco spokesperson defended the company's lamb stocking policy. "We are dedicated to providing our customers with the finest local and regional produce that Scotland has to offer. This includes stocking 100% Scotch lamb in our Finest range in our Scottish stores from June to December, when Scotch lamb is in season, and using Scotch lamb year-round for our core Tesco-branded lamb products." The memo also cautions of a potential assault on nearby Togo. Neither Ghana nor Togo have previously been subjected to attacks by militant Islamists. The first such incident in Ivory Coast transpired on March 13, when gunmen stormed the Grand Bassam beach resort, resulting in at least 18 fatalities. Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb (AQIM) claimed responsibility for the attack. President Mahama expressed concern over the media's leak of the memo, stating, "We must address this matter without instilling fear among our citizens." He also emphasized the need for public vigilance and warned that Ghana could potentially face threats from domestic militants. A memo, dated March 9, issued by Ghana's Immigration Service, urged increased security along the northern border with Burkina Faso, citing intelligence gathered by the National Security Council Secretariat (NSCS) suggesting a "plausible terrorist attack on the country is imminent." The memo further stated that the Grand Bassam attack, approximately 40km from Ivory Coast's commercial capital Abidjan, was likely carried out by gunmen entering from Mali, using vehicles registered in Niger, with weapons and grenades hidden in the spare tire compartment, wrapped in cushions and bubble wrap to maintain stability and minimize noise. AQIM has been linked to two similar attacks in former French colonies in West Africa over the past five months, specifically targeting hotels in Mali and Burkina Faso.
The Syrian Observatory for Human Rights has reported that at least five individuals lost their lives as a result of multiple areas being struck. The Syrian government and its ally Russia had temporarily ceased air strikes in mid-October to allow civilians and rebels to evacuate. However, Russia denied resuming attacks on Aleppo, stating instead that they had launched missiles at jihadist groups elsewhere. The Russian aircraft carrier, Admiral Kuznetsov, was deployed in combat for the first time, with Su-33 fighters conducting sorties from the eastern Mediterranean. However, footage from Russian media outlets shows these aircraft armed with air-to-air missiles rather than bombs. Government forces initiated a significant offensive on rebel-held eastern Aleppo on September 22, two weeks after imposing a siege. Since then, troops have advanced into several outlying areas with the aid of Iranian-backed Shia militias and Russian air strikes. Rebels counter-attacked in an attempt to lift the siege towards the end of October, but their progress has since slowed. The UN estimates that over 700 civilians have been killed in the east by air strikes and shelling, while rocket-fire has resulted in numerous casualties in the government-controlled west. Activists reported on Tuesday that the three-week truce on air strikes declared by Russia appeared to have ended. Warplanes and helicopters reportedly bombed the Haidaria, Masakin Hanano, Sakhour, Sheikh Faris, Bab al-Nairab, Qadi Askar, and Qaterji districts. A resident, Modar Shekho, told Reuters, "Our houses are shaking from the pressure. Planes are flying overhead, and the bombardment is all around us." Mr. Shoigu reported that a frigate, the Admiral Grigorovich, had fired Kalibr cruise missiles at targets in Idlib and Homs provinces, with the Su-33s on board the Admiral Kuznetsov and the Bastion mobile coastal defense missile system also participating. Sir John, in a recent statement, attributed the delay in publishing his inquiry's findings to the "Maxwellisation" process, a procedure that grants individuals under scrutiny the opportunity to respond. He further mentioned that some of these responses have led to new avenues of investigation. Lawyers for the affected families have announced their intention to pursue "further legal steps." Sir John initiated his inquiry in 2009, but a publication date has yet to be set. In his statement, he acknowledged the pain felt by those who have lost loved ones, having personally written to the bereaved families. However, Matthew Jury, representing some of the families' legal team, accused Sir John of refusing to set a timetable for the Maxwellisation Process, thereby preventing a deadline for the report's publication. In response, Reg Keys, whose son died in Iraq in 2003, expressed his disappointment with Sir John's explanation for the delay. Keys suggested that the witnesses should have been given a maximum of six months to respond, fearing the process has now become a "farce." Prime Minister David Cameron has also voiced his frustration over the delays. In his statement, Sir John defended the inquiry's management of deadlines, explaining that in some cases, responses required detailed and complex analysis. Clare Short, a former minister at the time of the 2003 invasion, questioned whether the Maxwellisation process was the real cause of the delay. She stated that the notion of endless consultations is not accurate, but suggested that the draft report may be of poor quality and extensive in size, causing extensive responses and potential revisions. The Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Select Committee, Crispin Blunt, stated that Parliament cannot impose a deadline for the publication of the Chilcot report as it would jeopardize the inquiry. On Radio 4's Today program, Mr. Blunt expressed hope that the inquiry would conclude within six months and called on Sir John to "bring clarity" to the process "as soon as he can."
Gary Coxall is set to take over as the club's chairman, following Ken Hodcroft's resignation on Friday, with Russ Green continuing in his role as chief executive. Hartlepool United, previously managed by Increased Oil Recovery Limited since 1997, finds itself under new ownership. In a statement to the club's website, Coxall expressed optimism, stating, "This is a well-managed club, and we aim to build upon the positive momentum from the end of last season." Coxall further assured that there would be no drastic changes in the playing squad, with the players manager Ronnie Moore had identified before the takeover still being the focus. Coxall added, "We are in a strong position to advance the club, and Ronnie Moore and Sam Collins [assistant manager] can look forward to our full support as they work towards improving the team for the upcoming season." The takeover occurred four months after a proposed sale to TMH2014 failed to materialize. Hartlepool ended the previous League Two season in 22nd place, four points above the relegation zone.
The Al-Madinah School closed last Tuesday, citing "health and safety concerns," following a single day of inspections. According to sources, the school was deemed inadequate in all areas by Ofsted, though a formal report has yet to be submitted. The school maintains that it was closed due to unspecified health and safety issues, rather than the inspection itself. Sources suggest that Ofsted discovered incomplete child protection records for all staff. Reports have emerged that female teachers at the school were compelled to wear hijabs regardless of their religious affiliation, and that girls were seated at the back of the classroom while boys occupied the front. The Al-Madinah School, a free school funded by the state but not overseen by the local authority, claims to be the first in England with a Muslim ethos, catering to students from reception through secondary school. The school's emphasis on strict Islamic practices has led to a premature full inspection. A statement on the school's website states, "There have been several rumors circulating, which is unfortunate. My decision to close the school was due to a temporary health and safety issue that has now been fully resolved and will not recur." The National Union of Teachers (NUT) has expressed concern, with spokesman Nick Raine questioning, "If there are health and safety concerns serious enough to close the school, then what were they and have they been ongoing?" Over the weekend, Labour politicians have urged Education Secretary Michael Gove to provide immediate clarification to reassure the public. The Department for Education is currently investigating allegations against the school. Some parents with children at the school have expressed satisfaction, with one mother stating, "I prefer the school to close, address the issues, and ensure health and safety, so my child can return to school without any concerns."

The council faces financial pressures due to decreasing public funding and increasing demands on services.
